<Content>You had better speak spanish or Italian This is our 7th vacation to Punta Cana and this one rates the lowest. We would not go back, suggest you try Iberostar, Riu or Grand Bahia, they are excelent 5 star and less expensive than this 4 star rated (really 3 star) resort.

<Author>DMSpin
<Content>Had a Great Time but the Small Things Bugged Me I was in Barcelo Bavaro Caribe Beach for 7 days (8/12/08 - 8/18/08). Let me start by saying that I had a fabulous time at Punta Cana and I loved the Barcelo Resort. The Resort itself is so huge and there is a lot to do that you'll be busy the whole time.Check-in for me was great and quick. While I was waiting to check in a staff member came by with Welcome drinks. Once we were checked in, a guy came by to take our bags to the room. I was happy with the state and size of the room. Every room has a balcony with a garden view and it was great. The hotel itself was so nice and loved the look of it. The beach was so beautiful and the water was just great. No waves and the water was warm the whole time. I took some great pictures but I will provided the pictures at a later time. I will tell you this much, please be ready for the sun to burn you if you don't protect your skin with sunblock.The pool in Bavaro Caribe Beach was the best out of all the pools in the resort. There is a section which goes down to 8ft deep, great to do cannon balls. LOLNow for the real dirty, I loved my stay but it could have been better. The one thing I kept saying was, the hotel would be great if the rooms were updated and the staff at the buffet exactly did some customer service. The real age of the room could be told in the bath b/c items that were sliver was turning colors. The bath towels should have been white and they were off white. The buffet in the hotel which was Buffet Orquidea, I had to ask for water the whole time. Once I was done with my first plate of food, and got another plate, I had to request for the first plate to be taken away. I could say tha the service at this buffet sucked. I wansn't too happy about that. Another concern I had was on the weekend, locals would come to the hotel and stay for the weekend. The locals were so loud, and would leave cups in the pool or on the edge of the pool all over. The staff members didn't move fast enough to remove the cups they left. Also, the resort is All Inclusive but if you want to eat or drink in the Bavaro Palace, you couldn't b/c it wasn't part of the package. In order to enjoy the Barcelo All Inclusive package, you would have to stay at the Barcelo Palace b/c then you can eat at the French Rest. Chez Palace, DR Rest. Rincon Dominicano, Sea Food Rest. Rest. La Brisa, and the Rest. that has food from Spain, La Fuenta. If you wanted to eat there you had to have the Barcelo Palace All Inclusive, otherwise you would have to pay $20 or $30 dollars to eat at the Rest.I did enjoy eating at Steak House in Bavaro Beack, Italiano Los Pinos in Caribe Beach, the Buffet Mirador at the Bavaro Casino which shares a kitchen with La Fuenta (hint, hint) The service in these places were great. We were unable to eat at the Rest. Mexico Lindo b/c the hotel is being re-done. The Bavaro Beach should be done by December of 2008 and would be the hotel to stay at b/c it will be updated and modern. I saw pictures of it and thinking of return Feb. 2008 and staying at Bavaro Beach.Overall, I loved my stay at the hotel and resort but the small things were bugging me. Would I return, yes but I would stay at Bavaro Beach. I say go, enjoy, have fun and to my ladies  gays, enjoy the hot men in speedo. (OMG!!! hot bodies in speedo, got to love that view. LOL)

<Author>GodsGift939
<Content>Won't go back I planned a trip for a group of 11, including myself. We booked 5 rooms at this hotel. I wrote a detailed reveiw so that people will be aware.Arrival: Parts of the desk arent marked so I waitedin line only to be told to wait on the other side of the desk for the same people to assist me. No one said welcome or enjoy your stayThe rooms: The air was filled with moisture. My room had a mosquito infestation. My cousin's room had a red ant infestation. The bathroom faucet was rusted and the bath shower head had built up soap scum. The water was hard and had bad water pressure. The ceilings leaked in 3 rooms in various spots.The Food: Morning was bad. The omelettes was the best choice to go with. Lunch, we never made it. Dinner, okay. The speciality restaurants tried to be americanized but failed horribly. The don't use real ketchup. Ketchup is marked kecthup or kecthup* - we never found out what it really was or why it was in quotes or had an asterik next to it. The do have to go pizza that was eadible. Juices were undrinkable to my toungue, but other got it down.Drinks: The most important thing while at an all-inclusive resort, right? Well they sucked most of the time. They used a lot of alcohol, which did the job but specialty drinks lacked. Pina Colodas were watered down. Mojitos had old mint leaves (not even sure they were mint leaves). The best drink was rum and coke - can't really mess that up. Fresca was a non-alcoholic drink that was good, but really sweet.Ceck out: No one cared enough to wish us well or ask us about our stay.Tidbits of info: Bug repellent costs $18. Go to the flea market next to the Bavaro Barcelo Palace for souvenirs. At the flea market, don't be hussled. Nevr take the first 3 prices they give you. They will seriously try to sell you a towel for $50, which you could get for $8-10 if you bargain. Book excursions early so you have a choice of days and times. Arrive on-time for everything. They are not to nice when you are wasting their time. Try to learn a little spanish before going in order to get through the day.

<Content>Not the Greatest Travel Experience This was not my ideal vacation, and although the resort is beautiful, the rooms were not the cleanest I've stayed in. My sheets smelled like mildew, as a result of the dampness of the room, and I believe I may have been bitten by a bedbug or two during my week stay. Guest services were not the least bit accommodating to our large group of 11. The buffet was pretty decent, but of course like most things on this trip, it could have been better. One major difficulty was the majority of employees at the resort who spoke very little English, hence non-effective communication throughout our entire stay. The highlight of this trip were the off-site excursions, but even these were ill-planned and slightly disorganized. I'm sure there have been many satisfied guests here, but I certainly am not one. I would rate this resort @ a 5 out of 10 and would not recommend it to anyone travelling to Punta Cana.

<Author>Allexie08
<Content>Not the best of holidays... We were 'bumped' into the Caribe at 36hrs notice after the Sunscape decided to close so we arrived not in the best of moods. Check-in took ages. Room was incredibly smelly and musty and in dire need of refurbishment. The TV and the lamps were broken, we are news junkies, and the safe stopped working immediately. (The TV was replaced after the first week and the safe was sorted within hours.) The manager told us there were no mozzies(!!) but we were bitten to death from the moment we set foot there despite every gadget/lotion/potion/spray/candle known to mankind. There were holes in the curtains and the bedspreads were grubby. The main buffet restaurant was a real do-it-yourself affair...you often had to clear the table from the previous occupant and then find your own cutlery/napkins/glasses whilst all the time avoiding slipping on the food spilled on the floor. There were always long queues for the beachfront bar/restaurant. There was building work taking place at the Beach Hotel next door with resulting noise and dust. The evening entertainment in the theatre/bar was pretty dire and repetitive. OK...the good bits...beautiful beach and gardens though the gardens could do with the litter removing! The room fridge was restocked daily without fail. The sheets and towels were changed daily tho the towels have seen better days. Plentiful supply of soap, shampoo and conditioner + shower caps, combs, sewing kits etc.. Proper coffee making machine with supply of coffee, creamer, sugar. Fruit platter and bottle of rum on arrival in room was nice. Food was plentiful and varied in the buffet restaurant, even for a vegetarian, tho it was a bit tired and picked-over if you left it towards the end of the service. We also ate in the Italian and Spanish Restaurants which were OK. No stomach upsets at all. All in all, it was OK but not a place to return to in a hurry!

<Author>houltonmaine
<Content>Good Vacation, Not the Best! I just returned from this the Barcelo Bavara Caribe (March 27th- April 3rd). Overall we had a good vacation. This was our first time to the Dominican but have travelled many other places in the world. Our room was the perfect location (6338) not far from the lobby, pool and beach. As all the other reviews say they are alittle out dated but honestly how much time do you spend in your room? Our balcony was great, big and quiet! The beach is beautiful with alittle sea weed by the shore. The food was good, better than I had expected. The only thing is that they don't change it up very much from day to day. The other hotels buffets are much similar so there is no sense going there. We ate at three a-la-cartes, the Italian- GOOD, the Mexican-BETTER and the Steakhouse-EXCELLENT! It is honestly faster to walk to most of the other resorts (Bavaro Beach, Golf and Casino) then to take the trollies. Its confusing at some places such as the pizzeria and at the food stop next to the disco because there are prices next to all the food items... these are still free for you! The first night we got there it was late and the disco was the only place to eat but we didn't bring money out with us so we starved until morning because we thought we had to pay. Lots of Europeans at this resort. I had read about that but didn't quite understand how many until we got there. I swear about only 20% of people spoke english and at the show one night there was only my boyfriend and I and one other couple from Canada! So if you enjoy speedo's and lots of toplessness this is the resort for you! Speaking of engligh, one big down fall is that the staff try and hardly any of them understand english to the extent you need them to. I would also recommend to bring your own mug or something because the cups they give you during the day are so small you need to refill many times and since there is no bar at the beach it will make your life easier! Also there are no face cloths in the room so bring your own. We did a few excursions. Every friday night they have a romantic lobster dinner on paradise island, beware you are not going on an island instead you are eating by the pool. We were disappointed with this but they did a wonderful job and the food and service was excellent. The cost was $35.00 per person but totally worth it. We also went parasailiing one day which we bought from a guy on the beach, that was $40.00 each for about 30 minutes. We chose to do the Reef Exploration tour, don't do it its a waste of money. We might have seen 30 fish and the there are 3 stingrays in a cage and 3 sharks in a cage. Not worth the $83.00 per person. One that we did and really enjoyed is the Bavaro Runners tour. It is all day and you really get to see the Dominican country side. As all the other reviews say, the locals are very pushy just don't make eye contact because if you do then they think that you are interested in what they are offering. All in all we had a great relaxing holiday and we would recommend this resort to others.  
<Date>Apr 11, 2008

<Author>BeachSpecialist
<Content>Wonderful Experience! My husband and I just returned from a 5 day stay at Barcelo Bavaro Caribe. I have to admit we were quite skepitcal and worried from the reviews we had read, but it served us well because we must of gone in with low expectations. The truth is everything was great! It took us a while to figure out how to get to the hotel when we arrived at the airport, but we simply took a cab and paid $20 (The range is $20-30). When we got to Caribe we were not disappointed. The beach is breathtaking, and the pool is exceptionally clean. Although the rooms might need a little makeover, how much time do you really spend in the room with such beautiful beaches and landscaping just steps away? There were lots of water sports included in the all-inclusive package (kayaking, peddle boats, and sailing boats), and alternating shows between the 4 hotels to watch at night. The buffets and restaurants always accomodated lots of people with immaculate service, even though we went during spring break week. Our favorites were the Steak House and the lunch cafe at Barcelo Golf. Tipping was not an issue; if you gave it was appreciated, if you didn't there was hardly any negative vibe. Like someone suggested on Trip Advisor before, take $100 in singles and $5 bills and that should be more than enough for tipping for your entire duration. Checking in and checking out were a breeze, and we were allowed a late check-out because we had a late afternoon flight. Overall, we had a wonderful experience and look forward to going again next year!

<Author>blackdogx3
<Content>Wonderful Vacation at Barcelo Bavaro Caribe i(Punta Cana) I just got back from a 4-day vacation at the Barcelo Bavaro Caribe resort in Punta Cana, and it was a great experience! Check-in was immediate, and the staff was friendly and willing to help in any way possible. The room was very nice and immaculately clean. The minibar in the room was always stocked and use is free of charge. The grounds of the resort were beautiful, very lush, tropical, and well cared for. It really gave you the feeling of being in the tropics. The beach is beautiful, and the water is crystallline blue.The resort offered plenty of activities, if you care to partake. There were exercise classes, water aerobics, water polo, dance lessons, as well as golf, tennis, ping pong, kayaking, and paddle boats. There's something for everyone. Again, the staff was very friendly.The food was good and plentiful. There were multiple restaurants and buffets to choose from. They offered 3 meals daily, plus you could get pizza any time of the day and there was a beach concession where you could get hamburgers, hot dogs, chicken, seafood paella, plus a number of other things.The drinks at the bar were free-flowing. They had beer and the usual mixed drinks, plus they had a lot of blended tropical drinks such as Bahama Mamas, Margaritas, Mai Tai, etc. Even though check-out time was noon and my flight wasn't until 4:00, they encourage you to stay at the hotel and use the facilities free of charge.I fully recommend the Barcelo Bavaro resort to couples, families, and even seniors. There were people there of all ages, and everyone was having a great time.

<Author>SOCSheridan
<Content>Barcelo Bavaro Caribe- Wonderful Experience My husband and I just returned from Punta Cana. We stayed at the Barcelo Bavaro Caribe. We had a wonderful trip. We part of a wedding group of 21. This resort surpassed our expectations. We, as many do, read the reviews and were a bit nervous but there was no need. The resort is a great place to relax and enjoy the sun. We left Halifax on March 1, just before a storm. We arrived at the hotel by noon, but our rooms were not ready until after 3:00. This was a minor disturbancee, but we were able to take advantage of the resort while we waited. We never had a problem with the food. We ate at the Steakhouse and the Italian restaurants along with the buffets. All meals were great. The waitresses could not do enough for you. Bars are available at all pools and beach areas. There are more than enough beach chairs. If one area of the beach was too crowded, we just walked a little further down. The Caribe has the best breeze of the hotels in this group. The weather was great. I never needed a sweater in the evening. We usually walked between the hotels at night. A train is also available. Our rooms were clean. They aren't the most modern, but how much time do you actually spend in the room? We went to this resort for a wedding, and it was beautiful! It took place on the beach. Cocktails and finger foods were served following the ceremony, followed by a dinner at the steakhouse. The photographer was great. The pictures were beautiful. We hated to leave, but we are definitely going back next year. We are going to upgrade to the Palace, so that every restaurant is available to us. There were a lot of families at this resort. Also later in the week there were large groups of students arriving. We figured that it was spring break somewhere. We were never kept awake at night due to noise at all. Security is everywhere. Hope this review is helpful

<Author>jennytollie
<Content>Paradise with one small flaw We stayed here from January 26 to February 2, 2008. It was the most wonderful resort and beach we've ever been to. We're a group of 5 and have been going on winter beach getaways for about 8 years. Always somewhere different so we've seen a wide variety. We really enjoy the diverse culture mix at a European favorite location such as Punta Cana. The beach is AMAZING! With the reef so far out we were able to enjoy the paddleboats, kayaks, snorkeling, swimming with the sharks  stingrays. One of us even tried scuba diving. I highly recommend the segways, we had a blast on them our last afternoon. If the ultra light very small flying machine is giving rides, do it! Two of us did it the first day and said it was 4 times better than para-sailing. The rest of us were going to do it later in the week, but it got too windy. This complex is HUGE with a ton of different things to do! If you think the beach is too crowded for walling, the grounds are beautifully landscaped. Be sure to check out the kink-necked mother duck and her ducklings over by the mini-golf. It is a beautiful resort and we really enjoyed not having to make reservations for any of the restaurants like most of the AI's require. The mattresses were much softer than anything we've seen in Mexico, that was a nice surprise.The staff work very hard and try to serve you as quickly as possible we felt pampered. I recommend two trips and will review them separately from the hotel. I only mention them here to say book them through your travel rep. We traveled through Funjet and Jerry was the rep at the hotel. His packages are the most professional, both safe and friendly guides with good language skills. I talked to people that booked 4 wheel jungle tours and other things off the beach and they were not happy. Stick with Jerry I saw him everyday and no one was ever complaining.There are two times during the day that there is no food available anywhere 10:30 to noon and 5 to 6:30 I think. We did find some sandwiches at the mini golf bar and the casino had a few open face sandwiches. We ate at the Mexican and the Steakhouse often and really liked the La Uva Grill had the best Paella and it's directly on the beach. Just on the other side of the water equipment. We never got to the French restaurant, but we liked the flamingos outside of it. The shows at your resort are above average and the Tropicalizmo is NOT worth the effort. Stay in one of the resorts where the drinks are free (or prepaid). We were booked in the Caribe hotel of this complex with a request for rooms close together. A friend who is a Spanish Professor called to confirm that our reservation was correct and stress the rooms close together. When we got there we ended up in the Beach (slightly lower rating) and in different buildings! Honestly though it was beautiful, warm, and just to wonderful to get upset about it. The only serious difference I could tell about the rooms were we didn't get a welcome bottle of rum in our room. We left a $5 tip for both the maid and person restocking the refrigerator everyday with a note requesting plenty of towels and cerveza. So once we got used to meeting on the beach in front our building or at the pool bar the distance between rooms wasn't noticed. All in all if we ever start returning to places we've been this will probably be the first. I've attached the map of the resort complex so you can see how big it is. You'll have to go there to see how beautiful.

Hard to fine english speaking people at the airport but communication is not impossible.Great for spring break / senior week........best value in the Caribbean, not the best island tho. Only 30% american, lets face it, American's are obnoxios and loud...Europeans and their kids are much nicer to share a beach with.

<Author>LanFamCan
<Content>Awesome vacation! We just got home from a week at Barcelo Bavaro Caribe in Punta Cana. Before booking our trip we checked out this site several times to find a good resort. The reviews on this one were mixed, but the pics looked great and the price was tempting so we went with it. I was not for one second disappointed. The motto I think they use at this resort is if it aint broke dont fix it For example there is one fountain that had two flood lights pointed at it. One of the flood lights are missing, does the fountain still get illuminated at night? Yes. Does it work yes, so there is no rush in fixing it. There might be the odd cracked tile in the floor here or there. Is it bad enough to trip over? No. Things like this are present in some places on the resort. But it is ok with me. Everything is functional but not perfect. This might be why this resort at the moment has a lower rating. The room (#6225)Located on the second floor a very short walk to the beach and pool. The view was nice, palm trees with just a bit of ocean peaking through. Kind of damp feeling, the air conditioning worked but not good enough to get rid of the dampness. There were mosquitoes due to the patio doors that wouldn quite close with out cracks big enough for them to enter but nothing we couldn't handle. At one point my patio door was jammed but they were very quick to fix it. It was fixed about 10 minutes after the complaint call.The FoodNot a single complaint. We ate everything and anything we could get our hands on and it was all good. No one had any serious tummy troubles or anxious trips to the washroom. We mostly ate at the many buffets but did try the Steak House (amazing) and the Italian Restaurant (also amazing).The StaffEveryone was amazing! They tried to speak English for us and if they couldn understand they took the time to find someone who could. They were friendly all the time and always smiling, singing and dancing. I have never seen such a group of happy workers. If you are nice to them they are nice to you.The ResortYes this is a big resort but there was a train that went by every 10 mins so getting around isn a problem. Everything is in walking distance so the train is not a necessity. I loved the fact that we could go from one hotel to another for a change of scenery and feel. Every hotel was clean and all the staff were friendly. The food was great at all of the restaurants.The PoolsI have never seen such clean pools. The water was a good temperature and no heavy chlorine smell. One thing I should mention is that the only swim up bar is at the Palace. We were really looking forward to the swim up bar only to find out we could not use it, very disappointing. No night swimming which was a bummer but oh well, there an ocean a few feet away.The BeachVery nice view and palm trees and almost white sand. Really nice.Most people don clean up after themselves but there were always men cleaning the beach. It is hard to keep up sometimes. But on the most part clean..The CasinoNolitours was where we booked our vacation and they said it came with $40 worth of casino chips. In actuality you get 4 vouchers for a $10 bet. To use the voucher you need to place 1 $10 bet along with the voucher and if you win you get whatever the odds were on the chip bet and only get the $10 from the voucher. I a little peeved about this but its not the casino at fault. Other than that the casino wasn bad.The Day/Night EntertainmentActivities/shows at every hotel night and day which are fun. The MC at our resort BirdMan as we liked to call him was very funny WOOOW and AAAWH AAAAWH is his trademark, nice guy. If you want to be pampered like a King/Queen then this isn the place to go. If you want good value, food, drinks, people then I recommend it. I don know what else to say. We loved our vacation and would go back in a heartbeat. I can wait to take my kids next time.

<Author>HollywoodMunster
<Content>Rather disappointing Our recent stay at the Barcelo Bavaro Caribe was the most disappointing of any trip we've taken. We booked our trip with our agent through Nolitours (we have related issues with Nolitours regarding what was included/promised  the representatives were nowhere to be found. Be very wary when booking the Cameleon Club Select). Rooms: We stayed in room 6256, oceanview. What we weren't told was that this room would be an add'l US $35.00/night. The room, though basically clean, was stuck somewhere in the late 1970's. Initially, our TV did not work at all  the staff was actually quick to change it out completely. We found bugs in our room 3 nights in a row and complained 3 nights in a row. It wasn't until my husband threw a fit at the front desk that someone actually arrived  sprayed our room. After that we only found the odd creepy crawly. Our balcony had a great view of the beach and the ocean, but it also has a pigeon living in the rafter, so EVERY day there was MASSIVE pigeon poop on our balcony. Rather then fix the gap in the rafter, I guess they would rather the maid mop it daily.Food: The food was mostly typical buffet fare. We mainly ate at the Caribe Buffet for breakfast  lunch, although we did go once to the Beach buffet for breakfast (seemed very small and chaotic vs. Caribe). My tenderloin medallions were good, but also under cooked at the steakhouse. My husband said his burger was disgusting. The tequila shrimp  taco bar at the Mexican restaurant and the pizza from the Italian restaurants are probably the best food served here. Beach/Pools/Grounds: The beach was fantastic white powdery sand and the water clear (probably the best thing going for the hotel). The chairs were more plentiful at the beach, but if you want a shady spot, be prepared to get up early. The pool was typically spotless as the staff mopped  straightened the deck every morning (except Thursday for some reason). The grounds were just OK. The lawns looked like they need to be mowed, there was random garbage that wasn't picked up (we walked by the same blue broom head at the base of a palm every single day for a week). The grounds have so much potential if some decent effort were put to them.Service/Staff: The people working the hair braiding/massage huts were more then aggressive to say the least. Walking onto the beach or even by a beach entrance got to be a hassle, as they were CONSTANTLY nagging. Don't even say, Maybe later for a massage, because they'll come find you  hassle you saying, You promised! Also, have a couple rolls of quarters with you for every time you go to the bar for a drink. If you don't tip each drink, they ignore you. My husband  I are used to tipping at the end of a meal or day based on the service we received. We tip for fine service provided, not to get service. The front desk staff was OK. The maids  concierge were good. The massage attacks and poor bar service are foremost in our minds about this trip, it was really irratating. We did take a day trip Bavaro Runners and had a fantastic time. It was US $85.00 per person  a bargain at that. We saw and did so many different things (horseback riding, sugar cane fields, cigar rolling, hiking, coffee plantation...). This trip  the tour guides are bar far the most positive part of the our entire trip.All in all I think our money would have been better enjoyed elsewhere.

<Author>grandmonsterb
<Content>Good Resort for the money Stayed in the Barcelo Bavaro Caribe from Dec 20-25, 2007.Reservations: Booked via Deltavacations.com website package of flight + hotel.Flight from New York(JFK): 3 1/2 hours, no food - snacks only., arrived at 2:00PM local time.Airport at Punta Cana - fast going through customs, $10 entry fee collected before you pass through customs and they take away all the papers you fill on the plane/airport.Shuttle to hotel via Club Caribe: could be located outside, just turn right. They usually wear green shirts. Ride to the hotel in the A/C mini-van for about 25 minutes.Check-In: within 20 minutes, provided the print-out from the website with the reservation information, no credit card asked, got the room on the second floor, # 6108. The building is located next to the lobby and the balcony is facing the little yard. All the buildings are very very close to the beach...1 minute walk...Room: Two large queen beds, table with two chairs, 20 inch TV, CNN and couple of other english-language channels, but mostly local ones and spanish/german/french ones.Large bathroom, with separate room with a toilet. Great showers, hot water everyday and great water pressure. Good white towels.Regrigerator is in the room and usually filled with 3 bottles of local beer, 4-5 sodas(pepsi, light pepsi, sprite, etc), two large bottles of water) - re-filled once a day.The room looks kind of old but I could not say that everything was in bad shape or damaged...just it looks like it had few years of usage... The A/C was working great....a little bit noisy but working just fine the entire stay.Room service: every day around 10-11AM....great quality....I usually left few $$ every day for the maid.Beach: really great, white clean sand, lots of shade, you don't have to go early in the morning to get a good spot - plenty were available....you can go in eighther direction..the beach is very long...lots of space if you want to have quiet stay. Great ocean, clean, clear water, no rocks, great temperature.Activities: There is beach volleyball, some activities near the pool, but the activity team is not as involved as in other hotels I've stayed. Food: The buffet breakfast is standard with eggs station, some salads, potatoes, cold cuts, fruits, pancakes, pretty bad juices. Service is a bit slow...but you can go and get yourself a coffee wthout waiting for a waiter to service you. Lunch: lots of choices, some dishes are better than others, usually two soups, few types of meat dishes, pasta station, grill station(meats, fish could be ordered and cooked in few minutes).Also, there are several places right on the beach serving lunch: pizzas, hot dogs, hamburgers, etc. Dinner: The buffet is good, lots of choices, great white and red wines, local beer. I have NOT gone to any of the restaurants this time.I've also went to the buffets of other hotels in the complex: Beach, CCasino and Golf. Again, pretty much the same food choices.Food safety: I have not had any issues/problems with food. Use bottled water, I've also used soda drinks at the buffet, I've avoided some salads that didn't look too good. Entertainment: There is a show in each hotel every evening at 22:30. All the shows at Caribe were below everage. I went to see the show at the Casino hotel(Tropicalissimo). That one was pretty good but all the drinks they serve at the theatre are not free.I've also went to the Barcelo Palace to view couple of shows...they were slightly better quality....Overall, nothing to be impressed. The shows at Barcelo at Riviera Maya in Mexico were much better..You can easily walk between the Caribe/Beach, Casino and Golf - they are within 10-15 minute walk from each other. The Palace is away - about 30 minutes walk...so use the mini-train that is available the entire day and runs every 1--15 minutes.People: from all over the world, lots of europeans(brits, french, italians, germans, spanish), lots of south america(equador, columbia, venezuela, argentina, brazil), some canadians, some US. If you prefer all US/canada - this is NOT the place to go.Weather: really great, about 82-84F everyday, could rain for 15-30 minutes, the humidity is not very high. Check-out: no issues,12:00PM, ride to the airport with Club Caribe. Flight to NYC, 3 1/2 hours.

<Author>destreure
<Content>Great Trip Don't belive the Yanks Don't believe the yankees or brits. This hotel was an excellent choice for the price. We arrived 2 days after the tropical storm devastated the island and we were treated very well during our 8 day visit. My wife and I are from Texas so we know enough Spanish to get by. The way we feel is we are in a Spanish speaking country it is our job to learn enough of the language to get by. How arrogant can you be to say they should learn English to come to the US but why should we learn Spanish when going to their country. If you take a couple hours time before you leave to learn a few words like please, thank you, before you go I promise you will get a better response.I am 29 and my wife is 33. We both had a blast. This hotel, and this country, would be a good vacation for anyone with kids, anyone younger who wants to party, or anyone older who wants to relax and tuck in early. We went to sleep by 9:00 on two separate nights and did not wake up to a sound until 9:00 the next morning!!!The grounds were cleaner than any hotel grounds I have visited in the US or tropics. They entire hotel staff is dedicated to creating a clean environment. I watched a security guard pick up trash as he made his nightly rounds.  The hotel food is good (NOT EXCELLENT) But good.The rooms were Good. (Again not Excellent).The beach.. OMG. What else can you say about a perfect caribbean beach with the clearest blue water in the world. I can't imagine a beach cleaner or more beautiful in the entire world. Remember this is a beach vacation and you will enjoy your stay.The drinks were great. If you did not ask for alcohol they did not serve it. They are a family resort. Kids order pina colada's all day long. They would rather not give some drunk yankee rum than give a child alcohol. If you want rum just order your drink and say WITH RUM. Or in spanish.. CON RUM. That simple. No reason to complain. because you didn't get something you didn't ask for. The service was ok. The service in NY is 10 times worse than the worst service I recieved in the Dominican. Some staff was less than friendly but once you initiated conversation they were all willing to help. We took an 8 hour day trip with Bavaro Runners. This is a must for anyone interested in learning about the country you are visiting. This trip was reasonably priced (80 US per Person). It included drinks (RUM AND CERVAZA), lunch and a wealth of knowledge. We visited the local farms, churches, schools, etc. We were pretty tired by the end of the day but it was well worth the time out away from the beach.This is a must do trip for anyone looking for a quiet relaxing time away from reality.

<Content>Very nice place, really Caribbean! We've been twice times to Barcelo Bavaro Beach Resort. Every time I am reading people are rude, the staff, and the Europeans are rude... Would it not be nice and honest if you look at yourself and think in what way you are acting and how you behave? Think about that please. Looking not nice, because you've a bad day/hangover of too much alcohol the night before? And because of that, puking in the pool? We've seen it happen and did feel bad about it.A lot of tourists tell you to tipp the maid, the waiters and so on... But please also think of the people who are gardening for you, in the heat of the sun whole day, 6 days a week. With one or two dollars or a bottle of water, they are very happy wiht it. And also the man on the train(s), they don't get anything except their salary. Most of the time they are forgotten by the tourists. One man was writing about the wet slippery and often hot tiles. So sorry, but I must laugh about that. If you walk around and they don't clean everything, than people complain. The tiles are too hot? Tip: wear open shoes (flipflops) so your feet don't get burned!All in all, we like the resort very much. We hope to return to BBB in april or may 2008. The shows are fine, the whole complex looks like a small village. The food is good, the staff is behaving normal seeing the circumstances.A lot of the staf get very low paid, around $150,- a month, working 6 days a week, or even more, because most of them collect their free days and go off for 4 days a month to see their family. Can you imagine, working more than 12 ours a day every day?? In that heat. I would not think of it! They don't want to be friends with you. That's reality. All they want is their job, get the money, have some fun with their real friends and family (very important to them!) and have some sleep...... Maybe they want the same things as you expect at your work at home? Why must that be a problem?There are also complaints that the staff cannot or are not willing to speak English. When we speak to them, broken Spanish and in English, they told us that the management don't want them to follow English courses, because than they (the management) have to pay them more salary. I heard it in the Dom.Rep. and also at Brasil (their language there is Portugese). So don't blame the staff, but (most of the time) the European! or American management.I must agree with some other people: we are guests in a 3th world country, so you cannot wish having everything the same as it is in your country. If you want to have that luxury and a more than 100% (fake-smile)service, than go on holiday in your own country or stay at home.The smell in the room: when it is humid and hot, put on the a.c. when you get in the room and if you like, at night. Maybe it will go away if you do so.The resort is old (I think now around 15 years). Because of the heat and the sea, everything gets old in a fast way. As I heard from my travelagency and read from other people on other websites, they are renewing the Beach-part. Maybe later the other sections will be renewed? If you choose this accomodation, don't worry, you will get what you've paid for. It is worth the money.

<Author>xsinister1x
<Content>Decent trip overall Buffett service is slow, it seems like the service staff per table is 9 to 1, meaning one service staff per 9 tables. So expect filling and re-filling of water to be slow. Get yourself fruit drinks, colas, beer, wine, etc yourself to speed up the thirst quenching process. Lots of food varieties, I recommend the fresh cooked section whereas they'll cook your eggs or omlette in front of you using real eggs not powdered eggs. During lunch, use this area too if you're food picky, as you can get grilled chicken, beef skirt steaks, and fish fillets cooked in front of you. If you prefer buffett style, numerous options to choose from. Pizza at many of the restaurants is ok do not confuse this with your favorite pizza eatery from home, but definitely do-able. Check out the Bavaro Steakhouse, which is included in the all-inclusive price - the Churrasco and the Sirloin cuts are worth getting. Both are better than average beef skirt cuts, but well tenderized in sea water which leaves a good taste - not too salty and brings out the taste surprisingly well. (Skirt steak is a cheaper cut, but if marinated right it can be very good). The Italian restaurant is ok and the Mexican Lindo is ok as well - had good table service at each, but the food is avg so it only gets the ok grading. Pool bar service can be slow, I found it's always faster if you want to the bar area where the beverage is located - for example if you want bottled water, move to the section of the bar that stores it in the area, same for other types of drinks. Most alcohol drinks are watered down - I expected that, plus they cannot make a Mojito if their life depended on it - don't even ask for this drink you'd be wasting your time. The cash bar is decently priced, but don't expect a huge variety like at your favorite watering hole. La Uva beach bar had rude and slow service, did it once and that was enough for me. Barcelo Bavaro Caribe has by far better landscaping than Bavaro Golf, Barvaro Casino and Bavaro Beach, the grounds looked great. The rooms were average, the ac leaked water from the ceiling during the overnight but it was taken care of the next morning. The ac does get cold, very very cold. Shower water pressure was avg, but usable. House keeping did a good job on cleaning and re-stocking the in-roon minibar (drinking the glass bottled Cokes tasted so much better than the canned Cokes here in the U.S.). They took care of the beach, raked it each morning to rid the seawood and debris - walk the beach and see other resort properties and compare, you should see the difference on how well Barcelo took care of it's beach maintenance. The pool was in good shape, even with large crowds. All in all, I would go back.

<Author>MLMD
<Content>Decent hotel, Best beach, bad food My girlfriends and I stayed here in May 2006. We had a WONDERFUL time, but that doesn't mean the hotel is terrific. Hotel was decent. Rooms were decent, but not on par with most U.S. hotels (regular hotels like Marriott, etc.; not Motel 6). We didn't stay in the rooms much. Small problem with tiny ants in our room. They didn't bother us, but got into our luggage, so we had to knock them out. Bathroom isn't that great and very dimly lit, but we didn't care. The beach was absolutely breathtaking. Perfect crystal clear water that is shallow for a good distance from the shore. Nice pool, but who wants to be at the pool when there's the beach? The beach water is so calm and perfect you don't need the pool. We found the staff friendly. The food, however, was horrible. The only food we liked was the fruit and the pizzas offered at the small pizza shack by the pool. Buffet was awful, but the worst was the Italian restaurant by far. Take advantage of the tour guide at the hotel. We booked the Marinarium tour (boat takes you out to snorkel w/ nurse sharks  rays and then for a dip in chest deep water where they serve you drinks in the ocean). The Marinarium tour was FABULOUS! Highly recommend it! You'll miss out if you don't go! The staff on the tour were the best!!! Lots of fun! Anyways, if you're looking for great free food, then forget about this place. But, if you're more into the beach, then this is your place! We loved it!

<Author>sandrich
<Content>Many misleading reviews We spent 2 great weeks at the Barcelo Bavaro Caribe and I really wonder what caused so many negative reviews. What do people expect at a 3 1/2 star resort outside of Canada or the U.S. ? The best review was written by craigggg, Halifax. He was there just 2 weeks before us and saw and experienced just what we did. I just would like to add a bit more. The pool (at the deep section) was 50 meters long and large black tiles enabled you to swim in a straight line. I am a competitive swimmer and swam for 40 min. at 8:00 a.m. totally alone every day that I wasn't scuba diving or taking a land excusion. I have travelled extensively and have never experienced that. Scuba diving is offered(for $ ) next door at the Barcelo Beach. The company, Scuba Caribe, is first class, offers instruction and has good Divemasters and boats. The diving is beyond the barrier reef so be prepared for top side swells of 10 feet and quite a surge beneath. Many were getting seasick on a calm day, so beware. We booked 3 land (sea) excursions through the Transat reps, Valerie and Patrick. These two are great and so very helpful. Do'nt go out on your own... While there, be generous with tips, learn a few phrases of Spanish (we speak Spanish fairly well) if you want better service. Have a little patience with European rudeness, which is rudeness to us, not to them, and just have a great vacation.Please read the review by craigggg, Halifax, Feb. 19th '07

<Author>luv2travel85
<Content>It was OK... I travelled to DR in June of 2006 with 4 couples total. First of all we were supposed to be booked at the Beach hotel but forsome reason our agent didn't do that and so I was totally expecting something different.The check in was quick for everyone and they kept our rooms all right next door to each other so that was great. The beach is totallyworth it because it is lined with palm trees and i believe it is the last resort on that side of the island. The rooms we small and the beds are hard but I'm not that picky because we didnt spend much time in there anyways. Housekeeping nevercame the same time everyday. sometimes at like 8 am (im young!! i like to sleep in!!) and we would send her away and other times she would come at like 5pm (bad timing since this was when we would come back from the beach and would want to get ready for dinner). I would always leave something for her though and she would give us extra towels and coffee (im not a coffee drinker but if u like strong coffee, stock up on the ones they give u in the room and you can buy the same at the flea market by the Palace side ) We only made it to breakfast twice b/c they stopped serving at like 9 or 930 and we would have to eat the rolls and ham and cheese with Juice that was left by the bar for the late people (although it was not that bad) lunch was always at the pizzeria. it was ok but after a few days its annoying. Dinner was either at our buffet restaurant (which was OK), the Golf buffet rest.(def good selections!!), or the casino buffet ( the best selection!!), or the mexican restaurant (buffet here is good, the meals you order are OK). We never ate at the Beach's buffet. Im not a picky eater but we had a girl who was pregnant and was told by her Dr. not to eat anything fried and she didnt have any troubles finding something good to eat. I only wich they had more Dominican food b/c Ive heard its very tasty. The drinks were good anywhere. We all liked the Fanta b/c it was ok to drink it flat. All the soda there is flat by the way. Don't drink too many Miami Vices they will upset your stomach and do try some other drinks like a Mojito or a Caipirinha, very good. The Disco is horrible. it smells really bad and it was really crowded and everyone is sweating b/c ther is no AC in there. We went there once and then never went back b.c it was awful. Although if your looking for a late night snack, go around the disco and you will find a little place on the side of the bulding that makes really good cheese burgers. Just ask for more than one when you order b/c they are really small. Usually went to the shows at our hotel. They are pretty funny and entertaining. Heard Tropicalissimo is good but i left really b/c i got a fever for some unknown reason ( i was OK once i took some Benedryl). Definitley get a massage on the beach, its worth every penny. If you want to go parasailing or on a banana boat ride book it at teh end of the palace hotel b/c it is a lot cheaper. We paid 15 US a person for a 30 min banana boat ride (at resort they wanted 25 US a person for a 20 min ride) and parasailing was 60 a person. The pool is nice but too hot b/c the palm trees prevent any breeze from coming by the pool area. The beach was def the place to be b/c even though it was really hot and humid there was always a breeze going by. The water is absolutely amazing!! I have never been to the caribbean but its even more beautiful once you see it in person. I would def go back to the DR but will not stay at the Barcelo Bavaro or any other Barcelo REsort. The entertainment staff were great but the restaurant and bar staff at the Caribe didnt go out of their way to make you happy at all. But it was overall a good experience. It was my first time going to the Caribbean and I was trying to get the best deal for all of our friends but we sacrificed service. This year I did much better and booked a trip to Jamaica for a great price but at a 4.5 star resort this time!!

<Content>great place to visit We had a great time at this resort. We read some bad reviews before we went there, but we experienced nothing negative. <Author>J-J-Vancouver
<Content>Barcelo Caribe, Dominican Republic: A nice place, beautiful beach Hello everyone! We just came back from the Barcelo Caribe (Mar 9/07) we stayed for one week. I had read alot of bad reviews but am happy to say it was much nicer then I expected. The room, grounds and restaurant were all clean. This is the most important thing for me, so don't worry about that. It's not new, I would guess 10-15 years old but fresh paint and very open. The check in was a little crazy, a free for all. The staff has a real problem with english so the best thing to do is speak broken english one word questions.The beach is beautiful and long with palm trees all around and white sand that doesn't get hot. There are a few bars around so booze is quite accessable. The food at the buffets and a la carte restaurants was ok. I've been to many islands and well, the Caribbean is not known for the food. The best Caribbean food I've ever had was in Canada, as goes for Italian and Mexican. As it was spring break for the europeans there were many spanish  italian young people having a good time, we are the type that like a little more piece and quiet but it was fine. The Barcelo hotels are all located next to each other 5 in total Caribe, Beach, Golf, Casino and the premium resort -- The Palace -- which to me was no different from the rest. After speaking with a few people who were staying at the Palace, the Caribe was the best overall (ie don't pay the extra $$ for the palace). You have access to all resorts, so many people use the other hotels facilities. We did one tour the Bavero Runners and it was lots of fun -- highly recommend. We went to a coffee,coca farm, sugarcane farm and horseback riding on the beach. I suggest booking tours through your own tour operator so you end up with people from the same country you are. Enjoy yourself, we did. I gave this hotel 3 stars because we have traveled a lot and have stayed at much higher quality hotels but this is a great place for the money. Bon Voyage! J and J

<Author>Brandy56
<Content>A Real Experience and a Word of caution We stayed at the Barcelo Caribe (Prestige Class) Jan. 22 to Jan 29th. 2007. The resort was fantastic, the employees we found were very friendly and accomodating, noting like the negative reviews we have read about.The beaches are the best with miles of soft white sand. The hotel rooms were as good as can be expected for a third world country, always neat and tidy although having the bar fridge refilled daily was a task.Only one bad expierence that made us concerned and very worried for our safety.We approached the Guest Services desk and spoke with an employee Yulanda and asked if she could reccommend a good Seafood restraunt. This employee immediately made a phone call and told us it would cost us $10.00 US to get there and $10.00 US to return.She wrote on a piece of paper the person who would look after us at Captian Cook's Restraunt.When we arrived at the restraunt a employee named Roberto was waiting for us .I asked him how much a lobster dinner for two would cost, he explained it would be $48.00 US.WE had our Lobster dinner along with a bottle of wine . When we were ready to leave and the bill arrived , we found the bill to be $233.00 US. WE were totally shocked and inquired why the price had gone up so dramactically.Roberto's response was that we would have to pay the bill as it was, we refused and things got heated .Roberto said we could not leave or he and his friends would come after us .WE gave him $150.00 which we thought was more than fair for the meal.AS we got up to leave Roberto ran out and instructed all the taxi drivers not to take us as fares back to our resort.WE were very nervous and asked that someone please call the police for us ,shortly a plocie officer came by and we explained our problem , told him what had happened , this police officer agreeded with us and instructed a taxi to take us as fares but that the fare would be $50.00 US. We paid as we just wanted to get away from Captian Cook's and the trouble that could have ensued.When we arrived back at the hotel I went to the Guest Service's Desk and spoke with Yulanda (the employee that set this all up ) I explained what had happened ,she did not want to hear our story and just got up and walked away.The lesson learned and to be told is that never leave the resort unless on a escorted tour with a group.Again the resort was fantastic, just one employee who is in the wrong job

<Content>I enjoyed my stay I read all the negative reviews before going down and expected the worse. I enjoyed the stay with no real compaints. room was cleaned to my satisfaction, always had fresh towels( a couple days they forgot to leave face cloths,not a big deal to me) grounds were well groomed. lots of staff. no real compaints on buffet service. they were always there to fill your glass with water( filtered) soon as you were finished they took your plate away. there was lots to choose from at the buffet but never varied from day to day which was okay for me as I only was there for a week. I heard lots of people rave about the steak house and denounce the Mexican restaurant but I found the reverse to be for me. My biggest complaint was the straws pushed into the sand at the beach and plastic cups left there by people(not the resorts fault) this spoiled the beach area. Time for people to be more considerate, There was lots of garbage containers around so no excuse not to use them

<Author>craigggg
<Content>Great place! Wonderful vacation We just returned from a week at Barcelo Bavaro Caribe. We read the good and bad reviews before going but took them all lightly as we find that everyone tends to have somewhat of a different experience when vacationing...very often due to their attitude and personality. We had a wonderful stay at the Barcelo Bavaro Caribe. The Caribe is one of five hotels in this Barcelo complex. The Caribe and beach are similar in many ways while the golf and casino obviously has a different but great atmosphere as well. People staying at the Caribe, Beach, Golf or Casino can enjoy the all inclusive eating and drinking at all four hotels..you must pay if you want to eat or drink at the fifth hotel (The Palace) of the complex. If you don't feel like eating or drinking one day you can certainly swim in the palace pool or lounge around the pool/grounds for as long as you want. You can always bring your drinks over from the Caribe if you want too. Anyway, the pool at the Caribe is just great so you might not want to bother. We checked out the other four pools in the complex - all were very clean but the Caribe was by far the nicest and largest as well. In terms of getting a chair on the beach or the pool we found that somedays it was easier to get one than others. Barvaro Beach is absolutely amazing! Just beautiful...very long, very clean, and well the white sand just tops it all off. I've been to some pretty amazing beaches including many from all ends of Australia and have to say that this is as beautiful as some of those. The resort has workers there to rake up the seaweed if any does happen to float in. The great thing about the beach is that you have the option of being around a crowd at the beach or walking down in the direction of the horseback rides to enjoy the lovely beach and scenery in a much more secluded area. The Caribe section is a little less busy than the beach section (they are just seperated by a wharf)..both have lots of loungers. The staff at the Caribe and the Beach hotels appear on the beach a few times a day to get people (only those who want to) up dancing and doing fun stuff on the beach. There are beach volleyball courts too if that is your thing. The kayaks, peddle boat etc are included in your package so take them out..The food at this resort was OK. They did have a lot of choices so you never had to eat the same thing for lunch if you didn't want to. We often ate at La Uva (right on the beach) for lunch..the calamari was excellent most days and the shrimp was great too. They had a decent size menu so I don't think it would be a problem to find lots of other yummies there too. We ate at the italian, the steakhouse twice and the mexican - all were good..no complaints..we did hear a few others at each of these rest. complaining about something or another..we just tried to block them out. The thing is if you order something and do not like it, don't eat it...order something else or go to the buffet and find something you do like. It was not the end of the world for us if we didn't like something...there was always somewhere you could go on the resort to fill your stomach..I don't think anyone should starve here. Oh, and breakfast at the buffet is wonderful..just don't miss it. The italian rest. has a pizza joint attached that is open until midnight. The pizza was a good snack when we wanted a change or something to fill us until dinner time. Sometimes their were lines for the rest. in the evenings. We could have went elsewhere as not every rest. had a line at the same time but since we were not on a time schedule we waited. We saw two evening shows plus the Tropicalissimo. The two shows we saw at the Caribe were good. One was dancing and the other involve the crowd and was quite funny. Tropicalissimo was really good. The dancing and singing was great. They must work very very hard to prepare. We went to the disco a few nights. It was fun..they played a combo of american and spanish music...our ages are 24 and 26...the majority of the people at the disco when we were there were under our ages. We ventured to the casino one night and stuck $10 in the slots. We tripled our money but in the end lost it. No worries. Just for fun. We read from many reviews that the service here was poor but we found the exact opposite. The staff here work hard and longggg hours but not once did we find anyone slow or rude to us. We did notice on several occassions that some (NOT ALL) of the spanish speaking people visiting the resort would order the staff around and treat them like garbage...We tipped daily at the rest. and buffet and to the bar tenders that we visited most often. They appreciated our tips and treated us well. We left gifts for the maid daily and always had a clean, fresh smelling room. The towels were replaced dailiy, the beds were changed and all in all the maids did a great job. The water pressure in our room was great and the water was always hot. The rooms are not the nicest looking but they are not horrible either. The balcony attached which will overlook the grounds or the water makes up for it in my opinion. We brought bug spray and after bite and they came in handy. Bugs tend to be around in the nights so use the spray as a precaution. I only had a few bites so it was not a major concern but I did bring and use Avenno in the shower and that took away the sting from the bites. If you have a trip booked to stay here don't be scared..go and have a great time! Try to learn a few spanish phrases before you go. It might come in handy. Most of the staff understandes basic english and some menus are in english but it is always nice to make a little attempt to use their language. The markets down the beach past the palace seemed to be the best for shopping. Be prepared to bargain with them though as they start off with insane prices . You can end up paying just a quater or a third of what they asked for initially. Go and Enjoy!

<Author>kitty2006
<Content>Disappointed I travelled here from 19 Jan - 26 Jan, 2007, with my mom and 9 year old daugter. Let me start by saying I have done alot of travelling and I am very easy going. We stayed at the Barcelo Solymar in Cuba last year and I was very happy with everything, that is why we chose this member of the Barcelo Chain. Although there were some good things, I was disappointed and will not go back. I would suggest another property to anyone that asked me.The good: the food was okay, lots of seafood. We ate at the ala carte restaurants and service was good and the food was good also. We ate around 7pm and did not have a problem with any lines. The beach was absolutely beautiful and their pool was very clean and a good size. We had no problem with any of the bartender staff. Angela in the lobby bar was always very nice to us and when she saw us she remembered what we liked and would get our drinks before we asked. The entertainment was okay. There were a few nights where they grab people from the audience and get them to do some very, um, different things. Not something I wanted my 9 year old to see. We loved how you could travel to the other properties on the train, so it didn't feel like you were stuck in the one hotel.The bad: Last year in Cuba my daughter used the kids club a few days. Every day they posted the times and locations of where they were going and what they were doing with the kids. In DR, the kids club girl, who didn't speak any English, gathered the kids one afternoon for the kids club. My daughter decided to go. When she came back 2 hours later, I asked her how it was. Well she said great, they went mini-golfing. But, what the bad part was, no one told me that they were taking my daughter from our hotel, on the train to another hotel. What if she was hurt, she couldn't even tell the girl, since she didn't speak English. They should post or tell the parents where they take the kids. I would suggest to anyone don't go here if you are dependant on the kids club. On another day they did the same thing. This time they had to come back because a 5 year old boy was crying for his mother. Again, at no time were we told that they were taking our kids away from our hotel. The staff in the buffet restaurant did not talk to us once, even though we left them a tip. We sat in the same section everyday. We had to get our own drinks and we were lucky if they walked by and gave us some water. The last morning I filled out the comment card in the buffet, what a mistake. When I was done the girl came over and tried to rip it out of my daughters hand. I had written that the service in the buffet was poor. The girl then gave me another blank comment card and stood there telling me to fill it out. I stood my ground but was she mad. She didn't want to let us go without getting the card back. We left and we were leaving that morning so we were lucky. We could tell she was telling all the staff around us what happened, if looks could kill, we would still be in the DR under a sand dune. The room, was terrible. I have backpacked through Europe so I have stayed in very strange places. The room was never clean and yes there were mosquitoes in there. We watched the cleaning staff, when people checked out, we noticed that they never removed the duvet covers from the beds. So you know what could be living on them. The room also had a terrible smell like mold, I believe this would be because those covers are never getting cleaned. The airconditioner in the room is so loud, if you are a light sleeper you will have to sleep out on the balcony. It was always very cold in our room though, no problem with it working. The rooms are very small, I was happy I didn't bring my 2 year old as well, we would have been jammed in the room. There is no way 2 adults and 2 children could survive. I would have to give the room a 3 star at best. Like I said earlier, we were in Cuba last year at a Barcelo and it was 100 times better, for service and the room. I would really suggest no matter what deal you get on this hotel try another place. It is a 3 star.Another problem we found was that you cannot leave your hotel. They tell you outright that with our white skin, they will be all over us. We heard a horror story from a couple that went out for dinner. They were told $50 US for a lobster dinner and bottle of wine. This was suggested by the Air Transat Reps. Who I might say are more interested in selling packages then keeping you happy. Anyway the couple took a cab to the restaurant, 10 US. When they got there they noticed other people were paying as they came in. No one told them otherwise. When they got thier bill they now charged them $250 US. Well they argued and in the end threw down $150 US and left. Then they couldn't get a cab. When one finally stopped the waiter came outside and then said, the cab is now $50 US for you to get back. The woman was in tears and was worried they weren't gonna make it back. Again, in Varadero, we were never at any time, worried for our safety. We could walk downtown from our hotel if we wanted. And when we were downtown we only encountered very friendly and happy people that would do anything to help.The Air Transat Reps tell you to go into town and see Vivienne for jewellery and rum. They say she is the best deal going. We went and I think Air Trans gets a kick back for sure. There were no deals on jewellery here. We bought all our stuff at the Bavaro Beach Jewellery Store for a little bit less and the staff in there were great. Sorry for the long post, but I think I could go on and on. Again, I was very disappointed and I found I was not the only one. I spoke to several other people that were staying there and they all had the same complaints. If it wasn't for the beautiful beach and pool I would have paid a million dollars to get away from there.

<Author>QSuzzie
<Content>Wonderful stay!!! Mother/Daughter team just returned from our stay at the Barcel Bavaro Caribe Resort and we had a fantastic time (January 17-24, 2007)! This was our second all-inclusive trip and our first trip to Punta Cana. It is simply a paradise on a Caribbean beach - nothing compares!Here is what we can say about our stay in a nutshell:- House Keeping: rooms were very clean (bedding, bathrooms, etc)- Hotel service: we had the shower head break off the wall on us. As soon as we told Guest Services, they were on the phone and the entire fixture was replaced immediately)- Pools: all pools were very clean- Daily entertainment: fun to watch and listen to at the Caribe (aerobics, water games, dancing, volleyball, bocce ball - you name it!) The hosts were FANTASTIC! WOW...- Nightly entertainment: excellent time to wrap up your evening! Great laughs and some excellent meringue. Shows seemed to move throughout the resorts, so stay put to avoid duplicates.- You could save your time/money to miss the Tropicalissimo show at the Casino, as it was Vegas cheesy, not great dancing and your beverages cost you money- Buffets: we did try the buffets at each resort and all were good... preference = Caribe.- Italian restaurant (Caribe): good food/service- Steakhouse Restaurant(Beach): basic steak house... nothing GREAT, just good- Grill Restaurant(Golf): La Uva is a TERRIFIC place for your afternoon lunch (only open until 5:00p) Salads, CALAMARI and pizza are wonderful and you are RIGHT on the beach in the sand under huts- Mexican restaurant (Beach): you can order from the menu or there is a buffet which had EVERYTHING and was amazing!- Drinks: good everywhere - I sure wouldn't call them watered down as some had mentioned- Restaurant/Bar Staff: people were friendly and helpful- Brush up on your basic Spanish! English is NOT dominant there - you can certainly make due, but it is so much easier to have the basics- Resort Access: very easy access to everything on the Caribe resort as well as all resorts ** the train is great (every 15 DOMINICAN minutes)- Beaches: all of the beaches were beautiful (Caribe = larger/deeper, Beach = nice and covered in palm trees).- Tipping: bring your $1 bills - tipping is the way to go! Approximately $1 for buffets, $2 for restaurants, $3-4 for the maid service, $5 each night will get you good drink service!- Shopping: down the beach just past the Barcel's, there is a market which had everything - a must see and good prices/bartering!TOURS- Bavaro Runners: a rocky ride and long day but simply a perfect way to see the Dominican Republic countryside and the people (sugar cane field, coffee/chocolate farm, ocean, horseback riding, kids, cave) ** bring your school supplies/treats for the kids- Marinarium: we went in the morning and it was a little rough. Being novice snorkellers, by the time we were comfortable, it was almost time to go. Advanced group did go out and had a great time. It is a RUM boat that then takes you along the coast line - great way to spend an morning/lunch! The hosts were awesome!I hope this review helped you understand the Caribe and the other Barcel resorts!

<Author>dlink
<Content>Service needs work I gave this resort a 3 because the location, beach and facilities were very good but the service was very poor. Maybe we were spoiled by Mexico but we certainly noticed a different attitude for service here. We still had a good time and would go to the Dominican again, but not to this hotel.There are 5 hotels in this complex. The Caribe, Beach, Golf, Casino, and Palace. Out package gave us full access to all except the Palace. A train-like shuttle runs continuously between all the complexes.The beach is huge and beautiful. There is plenty of room and always chairs available. During January and February the trade winds always blow so there is a stiff breeze to help keep you from overheating. Good snorkeling is available right along the beach. The pool is more crowded but still not bad. We had one or two brief tropical showers every day. Not really bad enough to seek shelter, especially if you are already wearing a bathing suit.Rooms are typical of all inclusive resorts and since I don't spend a lot of time there, all I care is that they are clean, and they were.If you want good service here, tipping is essential. Rooms are often not cleaned until after 5:00 PM. It took three days to get a light bulb installed in our bathroom toilet.I know we were in Spanish speaking country and we used our limited Spanish as much as possible, but very few of the staff speak anything but Spanish. This includes waiters, front desk, and guest services people. It seems to me when you are having 300 Canadians showing up every week, that somone should be able to speak English or French as well. This limited participation in the evening shows and poolside activities.The food in the buffet restaurants was very good with a large selection. The seafood was particularily good and well prepared. Reading the item descriptions provided a good chuckle every day. (Soap of Beast translates as Beef Soup, Chichen Sald was chicken salad). If you want water, coffee or juice, get your own because no one will stop at your table.The A La Carte restaurants were not as good. No reservations were required so long lineups (45 minutes) are normal, and the food was usually not worth the wait. Drinks are limited to about 10 tropical drinks (which are often prepared without alchohol unless you specifically ask for it) and a half dozen standards. Anything else they don't have, or if they do it costs extra. DO NOT drink the house red wine. It is grape juice with rum added.Evening shows run from an incredible band with singers and dancers, to the usual men vs women fun nights. Unfortunately because they are all exclusively in Spanish it's really hard to particpate and enjoy fully.I have stayed in everything from 5 star hotels in Amsterdam to a dive in Ukraine where the chalk outline of the last guest was still on the floor. I tend to go with the flow and can adapt to most environments. But when you pay a considerable sum for all inclusive resorts you expect a certain level of service. That service was not provided here. Beyond the language barrier, the staff just seemed confused. It often took 4 people and 15 minutes to bus a table when 30 people were standing in line waiting for a table. This kind of thing detracts from the enjoyment of your stay. We had friends staying at two of the other hotels in this complex and they reported the same conditions.

<Content>stay elsewhere , not worth it, even at bargain prices Just returned from medical meeting at Barcelo Bavaro Convention Center in Punta Cana. A group of colleagues and I, were placed at Barcelo Bavaro Caribe Hotel. Upon arrival the reservation receptionist administrative part was a near mess, like a college admission event but not for college students. Got to my room after more than an hour, The room was basic, furniture poorly kept, had a problem with a lock and it took me one and a half hour and three calls to the Public Relations Phone, what a fancy name, to get help, with a frankly unpleasant attendant who could not care less, the third call was a nasty one and I got help in five minutes. The wall shower support was placed upside down, the toilett was leaking, I fixed it myself not to wait another hour. One of the two elevators never worked. Do take or buy mosquito repellent inmediately, upon arrival, otherwise they will eat you up. I checked for fumigation and saw a couple of clerks with small hand pumps once, doing house type fumigation, no industrial fumigation like I have seen in other resorts. Do not forget dengue is a reality in the Dominican RepublicPhone calls are very costly, buy calling cards accross the hotel at Plaza Dominicana Shopping Mall and place calls through them, cost is one fifth of hotel calls or less.Food is fair and no change through the entire week. You cannot use the facilities of Bavaro Palace, the more expensive hotel of this group, or have to pay extra for meals. The only good night show at Tropicalissimo required extra charge for the drinks which were not included. The rest of night shows were dull and poor, we did not bother seeing them after the first night experience.The pool and gardens are nice, drinks were watery and fair, ask them to add rhum if you want it otherwise you do not know what they serve you, the beach is beautiful as all beaches of this area are. Activities were practically nonexistent, played volleyball with a group of nice people without anyone in charge. KidsClub does not exist so forget if you think about kids participating in any activity for them.Personnel seemed tired, overworked, sometimes truly unpleasant, with very few exceptions. We had an argument with the waiters at the Steak House restaurant because we requested some tables to be put together for us and moving two or three tables was too much work for them, so we left. The only exceptions to this distant careless attitude were Roberto, an extremely pleasant receptionist and a youg fellow at the Internet facilities. The rest were just careless or frankly ubnoxious.The Convention Center was OK. The toilets were sometimes not clean at all, and the seats were broken and never fixed during the whole week of the Congress. The lecture rooms were adequate.It is my third and last stay at a Barcel Hotel, having other so much better organized Hotels I see no reason to return to this Hotel Chain where personnel trainig and good feelings, plus real passenger care do not seem to matter.Dr Roberto Balassa MD

<Content>Fantastic Getaway We just returned from the Barcelo Bavaro Beach  Caribe and had a wonderful time. The grounds were beautiful and the beach was perfect. We enjoyed great drinks (bring your own cup) and had some decent meals. The dining experience was alot of fun. It was alot of fun to try our the different restaurants and experience new foods. The staff work very long hours and are so nice. We seemed like the only tourists who made an attempt to try to communicate with the staff. They loved to talk with us and even tried to remember what we drank and what are names were. We also tipped the staff in the morning at the bar and later again in the evening at the bar. They are so grateful. The resort had a trampoline in the ocean that was an extra charge. We got the price down from $12.95 US for 90 minutes to $10 US per person for 2 days. It was great fun. We traveled with a mixed group from 22-50 years old. We enjoyed the beach and pool during the day, dinner at night and getting on the train and enjoying coctails at the other resorts.

<Content>Horrible My friend and I stayed at the Barcelo Bavaro Beach Resort in July. We were so excited to get to the tropical paradise and hop into the ocean. Well, things did not go well at all. I will sum up everything you NEED to know...1. If you don't speak Spanish, take someone with you that does because they do not speak English!2. If you DO speak Spanish, you will still get the same treatment as non-Spanish speaking people, but you can at least understand them.3. Customer service is the WORST I have ever experienced. Not only are they flat out rude to you, but they will intentionally IGNORE you. 4. My Spanish speaking friend got into an arguement with a waitress at the Italian restaurant because she threw the menu at her and told her to move her hands!!!!!!5. The Food is DISGUSTING!!! I may have lost weight on this trip because I couldn't stand eating the nasty (and recycled) food.6. I was not allowed to eat at the outdoor buffet because I didn't have my flip flops on. This was in the morning and we were at the beach...hello?? So, I proceeded to the nearest shop to buy some flip flops since our room was a mile down the beach. The ragged and cheaply made flip flops were $40! 7. That night we went to the steak house and waited for a good hour-two hours in line to only be turned down because they thought my ankle length skirt was a swimsuit cover! I then had to walk a mile back to the hotel room (no lights on the beach or sidewalks) to change into another skirt!8. My friend and I needed aspirin for the pain of being at this horrid place, so we went to one of the shops to get aspirin. It was $30 for a small pack of aspirin (non-brand).9. Don't expect good drinks. The alcohol is some weird Dominican brand and it's nasty!10. The women that worked there wear SHORT, SHORT, SHORT, black skirts. We could see their underwear!I've been to many places in the Caribbean and have never experienced such a horrible place. This was my friend's first time to the Caribbean and I feel guilty for having this place be her first experience. If you want to stay here because it's less expensive...DON'T. Spend a little more and go to another island. Perhaps other resorts are better in the Dominican Republic? I don't know, but I will not go back to find out! I hope this was a helpful review. I just don't want anyone else to go through what we (among other people) went through at this God forsaken place!
