<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Paradise on Earth We just returned yesterday, stayed from 3/16-3/21/05. I'm not sure what everyone in previous reviews is complaining about. They must be extremely spoiled people. The beaches were the most beautiful I have ever seen in the Carriben. You can walk for miles in either direction with absolutley no problems. The Complex itself was extremely well maintained, and loaded with palm trees. The food was abundant and tasty, no matter where you went. Service was great for those people that were nicier than those who expected it. A smile, hola, and gracias was all it took. Remember some of their names at the bar and restaurants and simply call them by it. You will be rewarded, and will never wait for a drink. It is not gourmet style food, but the fact is you are going to enjoy their beautiful complex, and the even more beautiful beaches. The rooms are very nice and cleaned everyday. It's a nice, clean room to sleep in, who cares about it's decor. Bring a larger themos mug to bring your drinks down to the beach. They stay colder, longer than the plastic cups. Grab your chair early in the morning to pick a great spot on the beach or by the pool. Don't expect to get a beach or pool chair if you were too lazy to get down early, before 10:00. You might want to pack a candle in case the power goes out. If it does go out, light the candle and go down to bar, no big deal.If you want to visit a tranquil paradise with beautiful beaches, this is the place for you. Especially considering the minimal amount of money it will cost you. If you want gormet style food, go to the Cuisinart or Cap Juluca in Anguilla, and expect to pay $2,000 per night. Food or Airfare is not included in that price. Yes, we have been there too.Your goal in going there should be to relax, and not stress over the smaller things. Go and have fun. PS-No mosquito's or stomach problems either.

<Author>sariavalaipete
<Content>Would never go back~horrible especially for families HELLO ALL~ I will start off by saying that I read a lot of great reviews before deciding on my families last minute vacation (and most of the reviews were really pretty good)? With that said, my family and I were not happy with the vacation at all and actually wish that we had not spent our money and time at this destination. Now looking back at the reviews, I can only assume, that most of the great reviews that I read were written by young (early 20's) either friends or boyfriend/girlfiend type situations where just having a cheap place to stay with a beach and bar is what they need. I have been there done that and understand :-) But we needed a bit more and didn't get it at all!!!!!!!!! We are 34, well traveled professional couple with 2 small kids (daughter' 2 and 6 years old). IF YOU HAVE CHILDREN (ESPECIALLY YOUNG KIDS) DO NOT EXPECT A KIDS CLUB OR ANY CONSISTENT, RELIABLE OR SAFE CHILD CARE!!!!!!ARRIVAL and ROOMThe arrival was smooth (weird but cool outdoor airport :-) I thought it was neat (even though it was terribly hot :-)Check-in at the hotel was smooth. The room was clean and small (with 4 people and me being a bit of an over packer) there was no place for the luggage and was really cramped. There were 2 double beds. It was fine and we didn't see mosquito's (which we were worried about with other reviews we read). We left $2 in the minibar  for the cleaning staff the first day and also $1 daily. Never a problem with either and actually the minibar was so well stocked we started taking the extra beverages out with us to give to the grounds keepers  security guards (they were very appreciative for a cold coke)FOODTHE FOOD WAS HORRIBLE. I have to say that maybe we are a bit picky when it comes to good food. We enjoy a good gourmet meal once in a while and do buy fresh veggies and high quality meats in our home. So maybe we are a bit picky but we have been to plenty of other resorts and have always enjoyed the crappie buffet food (sometimes the unhealthier the better tasting :-) But this was low quality  poorly seasoned. I really do look forward to the pig out buffet stuff we all get at these all inclusive resorts but this food was absolutely horrible and I truly did not find 1 thing in any of the buffet's or restaurants that I looked forward to eating. We ate at the Steakhouse twice and twice it was horrible. Next to the steakhouse is takeout pizza. The pizza was OK nothing special but nothing terrible. The beachside restaurant called La Uva at the Golf Hotel that is good. Tables are in the sand on the beach and it is only open for lunch.Oh and none of us got sick but we brushed out teeth with bottled water and rewashed the fruit in bottled water as well before eating it. We tried to be careful and no one from our family got sick (but we did see others complaining at the front desk and looking terribly sick).CHILDREN'S ACTIVITIESNONE! There was a kids club that was basically nonexistent they claimed to always be looking for the girl that was supposedly running it that day. When she was finally found there were no activities planned, she didn't speak English (so my 6 year old couldn't even talk to her). The worst was when I had my older daughter go on a walk to the beach with the counselor (about 1/8 of a mile) and 2 other kids we had met ages 3 and 10. We (the 2 sets of parents) stayed by the pool to relax and after about 10 minute we see the 3 year old walking alone and sort of looking around for us and crying. The counselor had just let this little 3 year old wander off unsupervised (as if on vacation there are no psycho pedophiles or crazy people). I was enraged that so little thought went into the child care. So for us it was a vacation with no supervised child care or alone time at all. Oh and it was funny telling my 6 year old to stop staring at the topless ladies (that were everywhere) :-)DRINKI do not drink very often and am usually a cheap date :-) getting drunk from one rum  coke. Even I didn't get tipsy the liquor is so watered down. My husband and I speak Spanish, tipped large and regularly and still couldn't get drunk :-) well let me say that my husband started getting tipsy finally after a few days of only drinking beer and lots of it. :-) LANGUAGEWe didn't have a problem because we speak enough Spanish to feel comfortable. But I advise learning a few needed words (If I had to use the bathroom, and the staff couldn't direct me to the bathroom because they didn't understand me, I would have lost it). OVERALLThis place sucked and we found a lot of other vacationers that felt the same way. I know it's cheap and you get what you pay for (yatta yatta yatta). But it is not cheap enough to be worth the feeling we had as we left thinking to ourselves we should have gone to Jamaica :-)

<Author>a_farmer_in_Lindsay
<Content>Beats the Heck Outta' Winter!!! My 20-year old daughter and I returned from a week at the Caribe for the last week of Feb. I won't go into all the resort details - you see my overall rating and I would just be repeating what others have said. You may notice that many of the extremely low ratings are from people who seem to have got a bad first impression - they arrived late and couldn't check-in (service tends to be slow) or they had a room right beside the noisy theatre, etc. I suppose I might dwell on the negative if that happened to me - but I don't think that happens to most. I would still say that the grounds, beach, pool are 4-star but the service, rooms and food are more like 3-star. And since we spent most of our time on the grounds/beach/pool, that colours my rating.One excursion that you may want to try is a day at Manati Park. The zoo portion is fairly lame (this isn't Marineland) but the horse, parrot and aquatic shows are OK. My daughter signed up to swim with the dolphins in the pool (along with 100 other people - 6 at a time) and the experience and pictures were amazing!A few hints: Take an insulated mug. You'll get bigger drinks and they'll stay cold while you sit on the beach. And DONT CALL HOME! The tour agent warned us about the hotel charging $2.50 USD/minute for calls to Canada. So we used the handy calling numbers on a card by the phone in our room to call home collect - it was all automated, should be reasonable, right? I got my home phone bill yesterday - $300.00 in calls - they charged $6.00 CDN a minute! You can use your cell phone in the D.R. if your phone supports analog. I used mine for a quick call - it was just like being at home. But I haven't got my cell bill yet. Take all the $USD that you think you'll need - you can't get any within the resort (unless you win at the casino). You can get pesos from the ABMs but you can't spend them/exchange them outside the D.R. so stick with greenbacks.In closing, if you're going to escape the winter and relax in a tropical enviro and don't mind going with the flow sometimes, you'll have a great time!

<Content>No Complaints - I would recommend it Spent Feb 19-26, 2005 at the Caribe and found the experience great. We arrived very late (between 12:30 and 1:00 am) and the service was slow and we had to hike to our hotel which was annoying. Felt comfortable and safe there at all times.You can always find fault whereever you go, but this location was great.The weather was good even though we got rain, someone cooked for me everday, someone cleaned up after me when I was out, I didn't have to go to work, what more could one ask for on vacation. There is no perfection when I am home so I cannot expect perfrection when I am away.

<Author>spaulding
<Content>The BEACH was great! Just returned from the Beach Hotel on the 10th. Had a great time!Weather: Gorgeous!! Was between 85-90 every day. Nice breeze! Definitely USE your sunblock! We used 30 and still got burnt. The evenings were still on the warm side- only needed a sweater due to the sunburns giving you a chill.Beach: BEAUTIFUL! Never used the pool- the beach was so great. White sand clear blue/white water and it was so warm. There was a nice breeze which you definitely needed because the sun was so strong. Very calm waters- kayak in the morning its like glass! Plenty of chairs to go around. Get the ones with the adjustable backs. We tried to set up as close to the waters edge because as the sun moves the palm trees shade the beach.Massages: you could get these in the hut on the beach - my boyfriend loved these and got them everyday ( there are no extras so don't worry ladies!)Pool- best time to go here is around 5 we'd come up off the beach grab our cocktails and watch the entertainment. This would go on until 6:30 the sun is still strong so keep the sunblock close (don't forget your sunglasses!) When the activities are done here move over to the hotel bar and enjoy some drinks and popcorn. Wait awhile before going to shower as everyone is doing this between 6-7 and the water pressure goes way down. Beach Activities: We loved the kayaks could go every day- take it to the point where there are no hotels (be careful as the point is an exposed reef and the surf is strong over there- we almost ended up on it!) The paddle boats are fun too. We took them out to the shark cage ( you'll see afenced in area from the beach -to the right of the dolphin platform) you can get out of the paddle boat and dive down to see the sharks- they are fully enclosed so no worries. Snorkeling is ok but you don't even need to wear a mask you see a ton of fish just swimming- not much color. Wouldn't spend any money on snorkeling or scubadiving as there aren't the tropical colored fish you are hoping for. take advantage of all the free activities. My boyfriend tried the free scub diving in the pool. The beach is great for walking- go left when you get out on the beach- you'll reach the mercado this way and then keep on walking to do some exploring- run into some local areas (women don't go alone)Rooms: were fine We had two beds one was better than the other. they were very clean. ac worked great (except last night the whole building went out - that was unbearable) The towels are a bit rough but we thought of it as getting exfoliated. We brought gifts to leave for the maid evey day and left a note requesting more towels on the first day and we were given 6 towels every day. We gave her $25 for a weeks stay plus the gifts. I also left behing some clothes that I didn't want anymore. The staff at the hotel has to pool all the tips so gifts are greatly appreciated!Food- this was the only problem- but we knew this going in. We brought snacks from home to keep the hunger away. Don't buy anthing at the gift shop a candy bar was $4! The restaurant we liked the best was the Steakhouse- then the Mexican then the Italian. The buffet is ok for breakfast but nothing else. The coffee and cap is excellent but gets you GOING! Drink lots of water!!! You dehydrate quickly and this will ruin your day too! Don't waste your money on the Palace food its the same as what your getting for free. We all got sick (there were 3 of us) Alot had to do with the sun and getting dehydrated- just be smart.Drinks: small but tasty. The beer is good. Bring an insulated mug and they will fill it up for you. We found the best bar to be the one at the hotel inside by the registration. Lourdes was the best! We brought her pizzas and she treated us like royalty- never had to ask for a drink she was always right there. P.S. they serve popcorn here too but you have to ask! Again they pool there tips here too! A gift they get to keep! We tipped her every day too and then left her a $20 on our last day.Nightlife: Not much. We did the Disco one night, the casino another and then did the shows they had at the hotels. We tended to eat late because of the lines for the restaurants and then being so beat from the sun the need for nightlife wasn't really there. We liked hanging out at the bar in the hotel- you'd meet a ton of people and discuss what you did that day and what tours were worth it. THIS IS NOT THE PLACE FOR SPRING BREAKERS!We had quite a few college kids in our building who were very loud! They really made a mess (ketchup all down the hall and over the walls - their rooms were trashed!) Pretty obnoxious on the beach too. There isn't anything for them to do but drink..Tours: we only did the 2 hour horseback riding. Lots of fun you ride thru the jungle and on the beach. they take you to a locals house to buy a drink - remeber to bring money for this and to tip the guide that rides with you. When at the house be sure to look around and play with her little girls and take note of everything they don't have (bring toys for the children) I have been to the DR before and did go off the resort and spent the day in a little village - it is heart wrenching how poor these people are and you will want to give them everything you have! The average Domincan makes $2500. a year! Overall our experience was great! We enjoyed everything the people were great the other guest we met were fun and great sources of info. Ask around before booking any tours everything is expensive so make sure its worth it. Give to the employees as much as you can and the children if you go off the resort this will be the most rewarding part of your experience here. Get to know the people ( learn some spanish or bring a book-you'll need it) Don't be afraid to go off the resort and explore - you can get a taxi to take you around for a couple of hours instead of taking a tour. If you just stay on the resort try the train that takes you around- bring a drink as it goes pretty slow. The resort is big but is set up in a circle so easy to walk .Everyday they come around to take pictures of guest with different creatures or employees dressed up in native garb. Take one with the monkey- he's soo cute! Its free! You can choose to buy the photo for $8 that night in the lobby.Would definitely recommend this resort to friends and family. Had a great time! Wish we were still there!!If you have any questions just ask! (Have been to Puerto Plata too)FYI our ages are 27,30 and 37 and we all loved it.  
<Date>Mar 12, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Don't be disappointed We were there Jan22-29/05 and I wouldn't go back. We checked in late and there was one person at the front desk. The service was slow and I am sure people were standing there for over 1 1/2 hours waiting to check in. It was after midnight and I had to carry my own luggage to my room and I had a small child with me. The directions given to me were wrong and it took forever wandering around trying to find my room.The beach is sandy, however there is a lot of coral rocks everywhere.The food at the buffet was the same every day. One day there were steaks on the grill so I tried one. It was the toughest thinnest steak and I eventually fed it to a stray cat. Many meals our drinks came after we had finished eating. The kids club was a joke. It was nothing more than a babysitting service with no activities planned.My room was close to the entertainment area. The music was so loud I eventually changed rooms. The buildings close to the ocean are all new, so if you are staying there ask for them. The room was average.The entertainment was nothing more than having some guests come on stage and participate in making fools of themselves, so if you are looking for a show, this is the wrong place. I am not the only guest that felt this way. I spoke to one man and he waited 1 1/2 days just to get toilet paper in his room. The outside bathrooms were disgusting! This is not even close to a 41/2 star hotel. The only thing I can say is the grounds are well kept, so on the surface it looks good until you spend some time there.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>EVEN BETTER THAN I ANTICIPATED I am from Manitoba, Canada and this was my very first winter vacation to a tropical destination so I have nothing to compare this to, but from what I have just returned from it definetely won't be my last. I am hooked. Had a great time in Punta Cana from February 15, 2005 to March 1, 2005. and was sorry to see my vacation come to an end.The facilities at the Barcelo Bavero Caibe Resort were fine. If I had anything negative to say it would be the maid service. As it was not always the best. You never seemed to get anything replaced if you happened to run out. One day we would have four bath towels and the next day you would get two, or you wouldn't get a bath mat or hand towel. Minor incidents. However, they could be enough to discourage some people especially if you were leaving tips each day and still running into the same situations as was the case. The Caribe Resort tends to cater to children so if you have kids it's great, but we were there for RR and didn't care for the fact that there were so many kids. However, the pool is great and we enjoyed swimming in it, but you had to make certain that you reserved your chair shortly after 7:00 am when the towel bar opened up or else you had to look for chairs on the beach and they were hard to find near the Caribe. The food was plentiful. The buffet's were spectacular and we never left hungry. We visited the Steak house twice and found the steak fit to eat. We also tried the Italian restaurant once, and ordered Pizza from the take-out, but we weren't so impressed. I think they could improve. On a scale of one to ten I would rate the food at the buffet's an eight. There was always an abundance of variety and the desserts were magnificant. I would be careful of drinking the beer. After several days of eating and drinking, something was making our stomachs upset and after eliminating fruits, oils etc. we finally narrowed it down to the beer. We quite drinking it and were fine. All in all, a great time was had. Take Immodium and ant-acids. A bottle of regular strength Tums cost $9 US and don't forget the sun screen and after sun screen. I would also suggest taking snack foods as a chocolate bar was $6 US. The people were great the weather was fantastic and one day I shall return.

<Author>awr1234
<Content>Excellent beach and vacation We stayed at the Barcelo Bavaro Caribe hotel from Feb. 18th through Feb. 26th, 2 adults and 2 children ages 8 and 13. We did mainly kid-related activities and so did not do most of the adult only things at the Barcelo resorts.Covering the different amenities-1) Beach - awesome. Miles of powdered sugar beach, you can walk as far to the north as you like (better walking north than far south), with gently swaying coconut palms and 82 degree turquoise water. Hotel has any type of water sports activity you want - non-motorized things are free (kayaks / windsurfing), boats / snorkeling trip / banana pull boat are all for a fee. You do need to claim beach lounge chairs early in the morning as they go fast. The waves are gentle on the beach as there is a coral reef about a half mile offshore that keeps the waves small. There is top optional on the beach and in the pool area (our kids kept a running tally - HA!). About 1 kilometer south, you leave the Barcelo property, and enter the Natura preserve. There are coral beaches there and you can venture out there to find starfish, flounder, coral (wear footwear or you will cut yourself or get your foot impaled on a sea urchin) and nice conch shells. Watch out for the quicksand-like area where you do sink down a foot or two (the very calm area where the coral beach just starts). To the north, the other Barcelo resorts (Beach followed by Palace), then the first flea market, where the merchants are rather aggressive, but friendly. Melia is just north of there, and the beach keeps going on and on.2) Hotel - the rooms are average. There is very poor lighting in the rooms (just two small lamps) and the beds are double size, not queen. The bathrooms are adequate and they keep the small frig stocked with water / pop and 2 cans of beer / day. One should not use tap water for rinsing or drinking, use the bottled water which is available everywhere. But that's not the reason one goes there, one goes for the beach, and it doesn't disappoint.The property itself is very well landscaped - lots of coconut palms, bouganvillea, etc. Has a definite Latin feel to it. All resort buildings on Bavaro Beach are no taller than the trees so it keeps the beach very picturesque - not like the high rise beaches of Cancun or Florida.The bartenders at the Bouganvillea bar near the pool are very friendly and they always had a crowd around. They have various activities around the pool all day. However, the pool, although it is very large and attractive, is not heated - the beach water is at least 8-10 degrees warmer. They have scuba lessons at midday in the pool. If you want to have lounge chairs by the pool, you need to claim them with hotel beach towels, which they give out starting at 7 am (we ended up saving ours for the next day so we could get chairs before 7 am). I suspect this is the norm at all resorts here. Several times / day there are parrots, or a monkey, or an iguana with trained handlers for you to take your picture with (they sell the pictures for $8 in the lobby). We took the horseback riding trip along the beach and it was awesome - the kids loved it.3) Food - The breakfasts were very good - good strong coffee (you need to drink it with lots of leche (hot milk) so to reduce its strength). Juices were excellent. Omelets were very good, and there is an assortment of breads / fruits. All the food, juices, and water is OK (it's distilled) at all Barcelo resort areas. Once you leave the resort, however, you are on your own.Lunch is average - you can get pizzas all afternoon and evening near the pool, but be prepared to wait a while around 2:00. Dinner - we tried a number of restaurants on the property. The Mexico Lindo (in the Beach resort next door) had excellent food and every so often they turned off the lights and gathered around a table to surprise someone for a birthday / anniversary. The steakhouse, also on the Beach property, had good steaks. We tried the Dominican restaurant the last night we were there (this is in the Palace) and it was excellent - it's not part of the all inclusive if you don't stay at the Palace, but the price was very reasonable, including drinks.They have nightly entertainment, usually dancing or some comedy-related activity. A very friendly, international clientele -many from Canada, Italy, Germany, France.They have a small casino, part of the Casino resort property, and it was active.4) Shops - there are a number of shops in each hotel property, and the Plaza Dominicana has many nice shops for browsing - they will barter for more expensive items at some of the shops. The flea markets along the north beach will always haggle, they really try to get you to come into their shops (give you a little something no obligation, mi tienda es su tienda (store), etc. 5) Mosquitoes - our first six days there we didn't see, hear or feel a mosquito. The wind was blowing off the water and although it was warm by day (80-85) the evenings would cool into the low / mid 70s, and the air was not humid. The last two days, the wind blew from the south, and it got warmer and more humid, and that's when we noticed a few more mosquitoes, as the air was from land. But still no more than a few, and no worse than any place you are during a summer. Overall, it was very relaxing, and the best beach vacation we've had. I'd rate the hotel rooms themselves 3 stars, the food 3.5 - 4 stars and the beach / amenities of the beach and resort a definite 5 stars.  
<Date>Mar 4, 2005

<Author>venus
<Content>Absolute Tropical Paradise! Barcelo Bavaro Beach ResortCheck-in: The whole process was smooth and they even served us fruity drinks while we were waiting. We didn exactly get the room we requested but it still had an ocean view and the other couple travelling with us were right next door like we asked. ell-hops?took our suitcases right to our door and showed us the room facilities. Rooms: The rooms were pretty good. Clean, with 2 double beds pushed together with 2 night stands, a dresser, table and 2 chairs, mini-bar in a pantry with additional shelves, bathroom with a separate room for the toilet, bath/shower, coffee maker, and patio with table and 2 chairs. Bring a travel alarm clock as there are none in the rooms and from past experiences you do not always get your wakeup calls. You get fresh sheets each morning but they didn change the top cover every day. They stocked the mini bar with 2 beers, 2 huge waters, sprite, and coke (regular  diet) each day. We had a partial view of the ocean which was nice and our building was pretty close the lobby. We had water pressure problems a couple of timest was if it had a mind of its ownut when it worked it worked well. You don spend much time in the rooms so we were content with them.The other resorts looked like they also had nice accommodations. The Beach was the most active and busy then the Caribe and the Golf and Casino the quieter ones. All rooms at the Beach have some kind of an ocean view whereas the Caribe had some but mostly they had garden views. I would recommend the Beach first and then the Caribe but both are still really nice. Grounds: This resort is huge and they really took good care of it. Nice walking paths with lots of palms and greeneryot much flowers but that could be due to this time of year. There were some but not a lot. The little trolley came around every 15 mins so if you didn want to walk you could easily hop on and off at each resort. One day while sitting on our patio we saw a grounds keeper way up in a palm tree cutting down coconuts. He noticed us taking his picture and cut open 2 coconuts for use was really nice so we gave him a tip to thank him!Food: There was a huge selection of food at all the different buffets. We ate at all of them which had pretty much the same types of food but there was still some variance. Don worry you have so much to choose from you won get bored. They had fresh fruits at all meals which were amazing and at breakfast they made you fresh fruit smoothies to your liking. They also made omelettes at breakfast and pasta and meats at lunch/dinner right in front of you to your liking too which was great. The staff at the buffets were very nice and were very attentive with your water and clearing your plates away. The door greeter at the Amber buffet in the Beach resort was the friendliest person I ever met! I see her at breakfast, lunch and dinner greeting everyone with a smile and she was very genuine. We only tried 2 a la cartes: the Mexican one had tons and tons of food. It had a mini buffet for your appetizers and then you had a huge meale were soooo stuffed. The Steakhouse had the best atmosphere but the food wasn as good. DO NOT get the ribshey were extremely fatty with less than 10% meat on them. All in all it was pretty good therehe other people I was with had the steaks and said they were good. Oh and the deserts were to die for with a vast selection to choose from.Bars: Service was a little slow at some but they really know how to make superb drinks! Anything you want! Premium liquors and imports were extra money but their not necessary. The cappuccinos were the best Ie even had! 10 times better than star bucks that for sure! The pool bar at the Beach resort had the fastest service and the nicest bartenders so we stuck to that one.Pools: The Caribe pool was the biggest and nicest. The Beach one had a cute little water fall. The golf and casino ones were least busy and were the less windiest cause they were far from the beach. The Palace pool was similar to the Caribe pool but there no point in going there cause you have to pay extra to use the bar services there unless your staying there (restaurants at the Palace are extra too). All the pools were very clean.Staff: The staff was friendly most of the time. Some spoke English like the bartenders and front desk staff but lots did not. It wasn too bad and we just accepted it. We tried our best to speak Spanish and were always treated kindly for our attempts even though they were lousy. The maids really appreciated the gifts we left and did a good job cleaning our rooms. All in all I found everyone was friendly aside from the exception of maybe 1 or 2 which were just too lazy to serve us.Entertainment: The little shows they have each night at the Caribe and Beach were sometimes good and sometimes not. They could be quite funny when they got the audience involved. The Tropicalissamo show was o.k. You have to make reservations at the front desk. It a really loud show and there are very scantily-clad women bustin?a move pretty provocatively at timesust a forewarning for young kids. It was an hour long but that was long enough. The Bavaro Disco near the Beach resort was pretty good too. It was a decent size with a dance floor, selective seating and 2 big bars on either side. Early on into the night they played older music for the older crowd, then European music and then as the night progressed the played more recent N.American music for the party crowd that stayed until 4am! It was a good time theree had a blast at the disco. The Golf buffet turns into a disco at night but we never went there so can comment on that.Beach: Spectacular! Wide, lots of beach chairs, fine white sand?paradise! The water was clear turquoise blue and had a little bit of sea weed washed ashore but there were guys who came and raked it up twice a day so no biggie. The beach was the best part! They also had beach volley ball which was tons of fun. They had activities every day but we didn do them (water polo, aerobics, dance lessons etc.). Excursions: We went on 2. The Kontiki Party Boat/Snorkelling was soooo much fun! Not good for kids but great otherwise! The staff spoke perfect English and put on a little show of dancing and they played steel drums. They were really talented and got everyone involved. The snorkelling was pretty good. Lots of fish but only of a couple varieties. Still, it was amazing. They served mixed drinks, beer, pop and some snacks. The excursion lasted 5 hours and cost $60US. The other one was the complete opposite. Deep Sea fish was awful! DO NOT GO especially if you have the slightest of weak stomachs. My friend basically spent $70US to puke in the toilet for 5 hours! We trolled for the whole time and only caught 2 fish (both mahi-mahi). Even though I wasn sea-sick at all the fumes from the boat made my throat burn and I couldn get that chemical taste out of my mouth for hours. Also for 3 days after when I would sit still my boat felt like it was constantly rocking back and forth. Unless youe a huge fishermen don waste you money. I was also disappointed the guides didn say one word to us and didn even show us where the life-vest were?scared me because we were so far out we couldn even see land anymore.Summary: I would recommend this resort to anybody! We loved it there and I so depressed to be home. I hope all of you have a great time at this resort because I know we did. Last year we stayed at the Ocean Bavaro which was also nice but the Barcelo Bavaro was way better. It had WAY more options and just overall nicer. No resort is perfect but this place was pretty close!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Week of February 14th 2005 We just came back from the Caribe hotel and were pleasantly surprised given what we had read before going. If any of the following drive you crazy, perhaps you should re-evaluate this vacation destination:*** Consistent, speedy service - the service is generally good, with large swings in consistency, particularly at buffet restaurants where you may waste valuable time waiting for tables to be set, coffee to be served etc.. Patience is a virtue.*** Sleep and Sitting by Pool - if you are not at pool by 7am to claim your lounger, you will be out of luck for the day. Option would be to go down to beach and bring up a lounge chair.*** A calm serene ocean - though the ocean is clear and turquoise, the winds blow consistent and strong. This could be a blessing in disguise because without the wind it is stinkin hot!*** Service in Spanish - very little language other than Spanish is spoken by staff. Even the front counter staff are unable to communicate in broken English.*** Constant Merengue music! Started to drive me crazy about day 4!!!*** Wine service: House red wine is served cold in all restaurants. YEECHH. If you want a room temperature vino tinto you need to order off wine list. ($16 - $30) bottle. Chilean Cabernet Sauvignon was good!Some other comments:Rooms: A bit old and dated. Much like a Holiday Inn in pastel Carribbean colors. Our room was clean and all faciliies worked fine. Small balconies, but large enough to enjoy a late night drink or morning coffee. (Yes - coffee maker in room.) Rooms have electronic safes, small fridges stocked with beer, water and pop. No hard booze. Room service prompt. Air conditioning is a bit noisy, but it drowns out all outside noise when set at medium. This was great because place gets noisy after 7am and when bar closes at 1am and drunken idiots start to yell.Pool: Large pool at Caribe and Palace, smaller at Beach. No place to lounge after 7am, but chairs and tables sometimes available to sit. Water cold, but refreshing. Few topless bathers. No swim up bar at Caribe or Beach. 1 towel card per guest, don't try to get more!!Beach: Nice long beach stretches from Caribe to Palace. Takes about 20 minutes to walk. There is seaweed in pockets, but lots of clear sandy places to swim. Water is warmer than pool with no wave action as coral breaks are about 1km offshore. Forget the boogie board! We found the best place to get a good lounger and peace and quiet was to the Palace side of the Beach Hotel. Lots of topless bathers. Teenage boys will have a great time here.Shopping: Stay away from hotel shops. Way overpriced! There is a Mercado just past the Palace where you can barter your brains out! We found starting at 25% of the asking price and moving to about 1/3rd of the price for final sale worked. If you do not get it right away, look in other stalls. The price swings are huge. Coffee is about $3, small rum about $3- $4. T-shirts about $5-$8 depending on quality. There is no town to go to shop in. Shopping tours were run into Bavaro, but I heard they were disappointing. Laramar and Amber are local stones, but good stuff is expensive. Amber is about same price in Canada. Beware of fake stuff. If you but at market, have vendor hold a lighter under stone to make sure it is not plastic.Entertainment: Non-motorized beach sports are easy to get. No lineups. We went kayaking and pedal boating to dolphin island. Bring your camera if you go on paddleboat. Great shots of resort from offshore. Night time entertainment at resorts is passable. Mostly dancing to Merengue music. Sometimes drives ya nuts! Tropicalissmo show at Casino requires reservation from activities desk at any of the hotels. Golf course is on site. Not a bad looking course (about 6,700 yds from tips). Cost is $60 plus half of $50 cart = $85. Mini golf is available for no charge.Tours: We took Bavaro Runners tour which involves open air bus to Cigar factory and shopping, house in country for look at local cocao and coffee making as well as cock fight (non-lethal). You can but cocao, coffee, vanilla, honey here, but it is more expensive than Mercado on beach. Stop for lunch and horseback riding or swimming. Finally to beach beside Secrets hotel for swim/lounge. As part of this trip we also visited sugar cane harvest. WARNING - this may not be comfortable for all. We were surrounded by dirt poor Haitians wielding machetes who started to beg for money, hats, watches etc. We were glad to get out of there...Our second tour was to Saona Island in the Carribean near Romano. Long bus ride (1.5 hrs each way), but beautiful beaches and a stop at a sand reef to cool off and pick up Starfish for pictures. You take speedboats to get to Saona and Catamaran to come back. (Or visa-versa.) Final stop at Mercado to shop on way back. Nice day and excellent guides. Both tours cost us $300US total for two people.Heard from a few people that trip to Manati Park is a real rip off. Just a few animals for kids to pat and small park. Cost is $25 which one person told us was $26 too much!Food: I was pleasantly surprised with food in all restaurants and buffets. We have been to 5 and 5+ resorts that had less consistency than this one. There are 5 a la carte restaurants you can choose from and buffets at all hotels. Some longer lineups at the a la carte restaurants because reservations are not accepted. Lines move very well though. Steak house at Beach Hotel was good. Steak was tender, but tiny compared to a good Canadian strip loin. Lamb was tasty. Mexican and Italian restaurants were not quite as nice, but they had good varied menu items. Buffets were busy in the morning and at lunch. Lots of variety, but by no means haute cuisine. We found it to be filling and reasonably tasty. Sort of like a Mandarin restaurant in Canada with a spanish focus!Final tips:** Bring a sweater at night. If you are walking or standing in restaurant line by beach it gets cool. ** Bring snack foods if you like that stuff. Chocolate and chips in hotel stores are robbery. ($12 for a box of Pringles!)** If you like coffee, go to Caribe pool bar. Great espresso and cappos all day long. If you sleep in, they have continental breakfast 10am-noon.** Load up on sunscreen - you will need it! WE used 30spf and still got burnt. Reapply often! Bring your own because buying it there will triple the cost at least.** Do not forget medicines. We brought Immodium/Pepto and painkillers and Aloa. These are incredibly expensive down there, We heard of no one that got sick other than through sheer alcohol poisoning and stupidity. We are still taking malaria pills, but we saw very few mosquitos. Got a few bites but I guess that is all it takes.** Take it easy and relax. This was not a Ritz Carleton resort, but it is good value for money. All in all the people are friendly, the beaches are nice, the food good and the drinks cold. ENJOY.If you have any questions, I would be pleased to try to answer these. ADIOS.

<Content>can't complain Just returned Feb 4 and was happy about our stay at the Caribe.I did research so wasn't surprised, I new what to expect.service is slow but that is their way, food is marginal, survived on chicken, stir fry, and pasta. <Content>GREAT GREAT GREAT Myself, my kids and a girlfriend stayed there from Dec.31 to Jan.7.05It was great - there were only 2 drawbacks i) the service (which I find on repeated visits to the Dominican is to be expected - but then again maybe it is just me!!). <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Loved it! We were in the DR, over the Christmas holiday and just returned to Toronto on Dec.26. Our flight was delayed 5 hrs.so we got to enjoy another night in this great hotel/resort. We went with our 2 teenaged daughters and they also had an amazing time. Bavaro beach was SUNNY, beautiful, clean, white sand, lots of activities on the beach and by the large spacious pool side.We found the Dominican people to be pleasant and hard working. If you treat them with respect and smile or say a few nice words of greeting in Spanish, they are wonderful back.(Ola, buenos dia, buenas noche, feliz navidad) Some tourists however can be very demanding and self centered so the treatment they get,unfortunately, is what they deserve. Everyone we met and interacted with on our vacation was pleasant and fun. A small tip for the waiters, cleaning people, masseuse etc. goes a very long way in this country where the wages are quite low. It would be a good idea to bring down some 1$  5$ and offer a tip once in a while, the Dominicans are very appreciative of small acts of kindness. We also offered the grounds workers bottled water and soft drinks from our hotel fridge since we could get drinks any time from the bar. The complex is like a small community with lots to see and do.We even went to midnight mass, xmas eve.There is a new caribbean style church on site. Take the little train which comes by every 10 minutes, until 4 in the AM, wherever you wish and have fun. This was one our best vacations down south and we are looking forward to going back soon. As a precaution against malaria we did take chloroquine.We only saw 2-3 mosquitoes. They seem to be under control. Not to worry, it's worth it!!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>relaxing vacation We were at the Barcelo Caribe hotel from Nov 28 to Dec 12, and all in all we had a good time. The weather was beautiful, the sun was blazing so use lots of sunscreen, and it would rain for approximatly 5 min in the afternoons. We love the beach, but unfortunatly we spent most of our time lounging by the pool since the beach was full of seaweed (it was floating everywhere!!) The Caribe hotel had one of the nicest pools, compared to the other hotels, so it was quite pleasant. As far as the service is concerned, we were very dissapointed...you felt as though you were bothering the waiters and waitresses, they would even avoid eye contact, so that they wouldn't serve you. As far as the food was concerned, you had lots of variety for everyone, we especially liked the Mexican restaurant and the buffet at the Beach hotel. But after being there for fourteen days we were craving BIG MACS!!! The majority of the guests we Canadian, and Europeans. There were also guests from Columbia and Venezuela, and they happened to be the rowdiest of the bunch. Everyone was really annoyed with their behavior (screaming, throwing their cups containing alchool in the pool...)Anyhow, all in all we made the best out of our vacation, enjoyed the beautiful weather, tanned, enjoyed the disco in the evenings, and most importantly, we didn't get sick!! Would we go back to Punta Cana? YES, but we would choose a different hotel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Was Great We went the week of Nov.27 to Dec.4We were overwhelmed by the resort when we first arrived, figured we would never find our way around. Was easy near the end of our trip.We were dropped off at the Beach Resort and then asked to follow a guy with our luggage, so we did and ended up at the Caribe resort but no-one told us what was going on. We waited a while and got a room key and our inclusive band. It turned out to be a gold band (very good news). Ended up with a 1st floor room near the pool. It still had a little balcony so no one would be right at your window. Room was smaller than others we have had in D.R. but had enough room. There were 2 double beds pushed together to make a giant bed and a couple chairs near the glass door. Washroon was large with the toilet in it's own room. Lots of water pressure, water got hot enough and very clean. Rooms come with a safe at no extra cost and fridge was stocked with a couple beers and some pop. We caught the fridge stocker near the beginning of the week, passed him a tip and asked for more beer and Coca Cola Light only. He kept it up until Thursday when we got a new fridge stocker. Maid always did a great job and we gave here gifts of lotions, perfumes etc. She really liked the light up Christmas pin and the stuffed snowman.Resort was doing a bunch of renovations and still finishing off some of the work due to the storm. Church was almost finished when we were leaving. They have a service Sundays at 6pm.Pools looked great but are cool (maybe due to my sun burn). Ocean was nice once you got in but there was always wind that kept you on the cool side.Weather was perfect with only rain a couple evenings and a morning. We were not outside at the time so it never bothered us.Got up near the end of the week early enough to see the sunrise from the beach. Sunsets were Ok from the Casino pool area but no spectacular ones.We ended up with the gold bands so Food was amazing. All the beef tasted like Canadian beef. Lobster was included and no limits. Steak house was great but I did get 1 raw steak near the end. Had dinner at Chez Palace, it was great food but very upper class. We had dressed up but they did not want to let me in with sandels but I talked them into it. We had 4 people looking after us. Pesto spagetti was great at the Italian but some of the appetizers looked a bit odd (beef one looked raw). Mexican was Ok but I did not really get into it, the pork shaved off the spit was great. Palace Buffet was great for dinner with Cavier, Beef Tenderloin, gilled meat section, pasta section and Japanese stirfry section. Breakfast was good at every buffet with egg guys to make Dominican omelets.Train was great, we just rode around each day checking things out. On Dec. 1 they got almost all the Christmas lights going, they had wrapped every tree from the bottom up to 6 ft with white mini lights. Wiring was interesting so we decided not to go near puddles.Beach was white sand with blue/green water, not too rough because of the reef but did have some areas of weeds.Made a few trips to the market on the beach. They are very aggresive for a sale. They start out with high prices and lot of stories how the US dollar in down so they need more money but we were able to make some deals. You have to know how much you want to pay 1st. Nothing is marked and prices are different each time. If you can't find what you want at the booth you are at they will run around and find it at another booth for you. Some days they would make the deals and others they did let us walk away. Did a bit of shopping at the 2 stores on the beach at the resort and they were lower pressure and you could still negotiate abit. Stores in the resort were way high and no negotiating. We did a trip into the town of Cortisito and it had a supermarket with great deals on coffee and rum but the main street was more like the beach vendors. Trip cost $9.00 each way so we could of saved the trip and paid a bit more on the beach but we did not know what a good deal was at the time.Casino was good a taking money away. $10.00 coupon is not much of a deal unless you wanted to play the tables and were spending a bunch of money.Tropicaismo show was great make sure you make a reservation. We watched Cats at the Palace and I enjoyed it. The other shows seemed to be audiance particaipation and did not seem to be as funny as other people thought. We missed the variety show but heard it was OK.HighlightsMet a nice couple from Waterloo. Had dinner together, went to town together and bumped into them around the resort.Did the sun too long on the 1st day without sun screen (wanted a good base) that is a real mistake. Not much suntanning the rest of the week.*** ASKED BONNIE TO MARRY ME Sunday night on the beach with an almost full moon over the Ocean **** SHE SAID YES***

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>hotel is beautiful, staff and food could be improved! We went to the Barcelo Bravara Caribe resort November 28 to December 5, 2004. We booked very last minute and spur of the moment (November 24th). The hotel itself was beautiful, the grounds were kept beautiful. Manuel was one of the gardeners at the resort and worked endlessly to keep the gardens clean. He was always eager to greet guest with a wave and an hola me amiga/amigo. The rooms were very nice and the fridge was stocked every day with pop and water. But be careful, the fridge stocker would come around before the maid and take her tip. We left a $5 tip for the maid on the first day, when I came back to the room in the mid afternoon, the fridge was stocked and the $5 tip (that was on the bed with a note for the maid) was gone and a $1 bill was in it's place. We found the maid and tipped her directly for the rest of the trip. The air conditioning worked very well and most nights we had to turn it off. There was a little lizard outside our room every evening at dinner time. He was very cute and I named him my little friend. The only food worth eating was at the steak house, the steak, lamb and hamburgers are excellent. Be careful eating at the buffet the food was usually undercooked. I had a hamburger at lunch on the second day there and bit into it only to discover raw meat. As well the pasta at the buffet was never fully cooked and usually served cold. If you have to choose between the italian restaurant and the buffet...choose the buffet! We went to dinner at the italian one night and walked out after the first bite, the food was not good.While there you definately have to check out the show at the casino, Tropicalissimo (or something like that). The show is included in the all inclusive package but you have to make reservations. It is a must! The shows at the caribe were awful and after the first 2 shows we skipped the rest of the shows. The host has an over powering voice and does not speak english. But the majority of the staff does not speak english and would not even attempt to try. Many of the staff would talk about the guests in spanish. The worst encounter we had was with a member of the front desk staff, we left the dico at 2 am on our last night and when to the other disco for a snack (we had been informed that was where the snacks were). When we arrived at the other dicso we were told that the chicken would cost us $4 US so we went to the front desk of the caribe to ask where the all inclusive snacks were. The clerk at the front desk replied to my husband with a derogatory comment that I am choosing not to repeat in this forum, and then refused to give us his name. Eventually I tracked down his name and the next day we waited all day for the manager to come so we could discuss the problem with him. He was supposed to arrive at 9 am, and then we were told 12, then we were told 3pm and then we were told that he might make it before we left for the airport at 6 pm. He did finally arrive shortly after 5 and we were able to air our concerns about our treatment.When we booked we were promised bracelets to the Palace (5*) resort on the complex. Unfortunately when we arrived we were told that the offer was no longer valid. Both the staff at the resort and the tour rep for Sunquest tried to say that it was our travel agents fault that the promise was made. Our travel agent is our very good friend and she was on the trip with us, so she quickly produced the printoff from the booking screen along with the phone number and name of the representative she spoke to at Sunquest before we left. Both of which confirmed the 5* bracelets. There were 2 other travel agents staying at the resort at the same time we were, and they along with several other people were promised the same bracelets. One of the travel agents was told on her check out that she had been entitled to VIP treatment during her stay and should have had the bracelets for the 5*, a bottle of rum in her room and fresh flowers everyday. Great thing to be told as you are leaving for the airport! After the 2nd day there the rep for Sunquest never showed at the resort again. We waited to book tours and were unable to because the rep did not show. I understand that isn't the hotels fault though, just a word of caution if you are going to travel with sunquest tours. The weather was great while we were there, it rained a few times, but usually during our evening siesta and usually it didn't last longer then 10 minutes. Often it would rain when the sun was shining! There were very few bugs at the hotel, I saw a huge roach on the first night, but after that it was a relatively bug free experience. I don't think I saw 1 mosquito the whole time I was there. Unfortunately the beach wasn't that clean, and there was a lot of sea weed.Don't buy anything at the hotel, it is very expensive ($8 US) for Pringles. There is a market down the beach, but the vendors are very aggressive.We spent a lot of time around the pool, but were disappointed to find that the waitresses around the pool would only serve those in the cabana, and no one cleaned up around the pool. There was a group of people from Dominica there and they made an AWFUL mess around the pool, food, cups etc and the mess wasnt' cleaned up. It sat like that the whole day. Not a pretty site for those new to the hotel.When we got to the resort I wanted to be able to come back and write an amazing review...unfortunately I am unable to do that. We have travelled to many different countries and stayed at many all inclusive hotels, this just seemed to be the vacation that everything went wrong. We didn't let any of the bad stuff ruin our vacation, either way we still had a great time, I just wanted to warn anyone that was considering staying there to maybe think twice. While there I recommend the Bavaro runners jeep tour, ask for mimi to be your tour guide, he was awsome! Also take a half hour and try out the mini putt, it was a lot of fun!Hopefully no one will have to visit the medical centre while they are there, but if they do rest assured that the doctors are amazing and are fluent in English and very knowledgeable. If only the rest of the staff were like them....

<Author>Ceally_Kay
<Content>Windy time at a very Fine Beach There were four in our little group; one being my 3 year old granddaughter who spent Nov 12 - 19th in the D.R.We booked within 2 weeks of our leaving and were assigned to stay at the Caribe. Throughout the resort complex there was alot of construction going on; many roofs torn off as a result of the hurricanes. The work crew started about 7 a.m. and we could see them working on into the night after dark. We suspect they were working hard to get the hotel ready for Christmas. One could find this a little annoying if you were trying to catch an afternoon nap but other than noise you were not bothered by the construction going on. November is a windy time of year in the Caribbean and due to a tropical depression the previous week this made for an even windier time. There were days when dark clouds scattered rain on us but they quickly passed by and we continued on at the pool. Most days it was too rough and windy to spend alot of time at the beach; until our last day the wind calmed and everyone flocked to the beach. This is a great beach for walking as there are miles of soft, fine, white sand. And when the wind is calm the ocean is smoother and you can enjoy some swimming and other water sports.The pool is not heated so be prepared for it to be cold. On the very windy days I could not get myself in the pool because the water and the air were both cold/cool. (It is that time of year - fall/winter and for the evening a light sweater is good). I found the best time was to be at the pool just after the sun was up. It seemed to be calmer and if you want your favorite spot you had better get your towels and chairs at that time. We had no problems leaving our stuff at the pool and going about the resort, returning from time to time. My grand daughter simply loved the water, whether it was cold or not. For the youngsters there is a play ground beside the kids activity centre with very enthusiastic staff to care for them. The Resort: This resort is quite old. Athough Barcello took it over in the late 80's early 90's, it put me in mind of when I travelled to the Caribbean in the 70's, the rooms are that dated. They are not as spacious as some of the other resorts we've been too; furniture, beds and bedding; plumbing fixtures, could do with an update. The staff do a very good job of keeping the rooms, hallways and poolside clean. It always suprises me how messy some people become on their vacation; littering all about.One interesting feature we noted that is in the enclosed water closet there is an open ventalation system above the toilet, between rooms. We were wondering were the funky smells came from !!Food: We did not want for anything. I would think even the pickiest of eaters could find something they liked. Lots of fresh fruits, salads and baked bread, buns and deserts to go with our cafe con leche. There were meat dishes - fish, chicken, pork, beef - whatever your preference. My favorite was the pick your own to be grilled and added to your fav. pasta and/or veggies. There are many choices of buffet or a l'carte to choose from plus the pizza is very delicious at any time. There are many drinks to choose from and plenty of water and juice for those who do not drink, like myself. Bar also serves tea, coffee and cappucinos. Seems funny but by the time the sun was going down you need something to warm up with.The Resort: Quite lovely grounds and gardens with many walking paths leading from one area of the resort to the other. The train was always there to take you around if you didn't feel like walking. Some of the wild life included peacocks and the Flamingo at the Casino. There is so much to see and so many activities, that you can do as much or as little as you like.Markets: We found that most of the vendors at the resort and the off-resort market up the beach were extremely expensive and few items had a price tag on them. It appeared that the price would depend on the mood of the vendor and perhaps how they perceived you. I doubt that the merchandise was even locally produced. At other locations (and this includes the D.R.) you could watch the local artisans producing the work. To us they were trying to sell cheap imitations at a very large profit.Day/Evening entertainment: We opt out of participating in these but there is lots going on. We heard the discos and the night show at the Casino, were quite fun.This is an enjoyable and beautiful resort to relax. The outdated rooms will not deter you. We had no problems with bugs; burns (use lots of sun screen) or being sick. (Except for the 2 other adults I was with, who I think overdid the cervsa and food one evening.) The majority of visitors are from Europe - England,Germany, Canada and the U.S. And although Spanish is the main language if you know a little Spanish it will go a long way. We brought school supplies with us which we were able to drop off with our tour rep. who forwarded them onto the local schools. Also, left little gifts for cleaning staff every day or two. Our complaint is the banking system - that some of the front desk staff had difficulty to change our American money to $1. (and we were only asking for small amounts and which they actually did have the change available.) As well, some vendors would say they had no change so pick something else to buy. So if you plan on tipping bring lots of your own $1. and stay away from the vendors; some of them are very aggressive. Relax and Enjoy.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Relaxed and Satisfied My husband and I made our airline, transfer and hotel reservations through Travelocity with no problems. We were in Punta Cana from Nov 12 ?Nov 19, 2004.Once we arrived in Punta Cana and were on the bus traveling to the Barcelo Villas Bavaro resort, we were told by the Prieto tours rep that our reservations had been changed to the Barcelo Bavaro Beach resort. No explanation was given. Once we arrived at Barcelo Bavaro Beach, we learned that we actually were booked at the Barcelo Bavaro Caribe next door. The owner of the Barcelo Villas/Village/Ocean resort also owns the Barcelo Bavaro Palace/Beach/Caribe/Casino/Golf resorts. To compensate for the hotel changes, we were given a remium Palace?bracelet for full food privileges at all of the restaurants at any of the eateries in the 5 hotel resort. There were several blocks of buildings at these resorts that were being either repaired or renovated.Let me respond to some of the negative reviews that I have seen regarding this resort. Being American, we were clearly outnumbered by tourists from Europe, South America and Canada. There were a few small language problems. But we were always met with a smile and the staff was very friendly. The room was clean and comfortable, with the water, soda and beer restocked daily in the mini-bar. We had clean sheets, towels and face cloths every day, and also received a daily English newspaper. The room and pillows did have a stall smell though, but I had brought a Yankee Candle air freshener and that helped, as did leaving the slider open all night for fresh breezes The air conditioning worked fine (although was not always needed) and there was plenty of hot water, even at peak hours. My husband did have to get up early to reserve chairs by the pool, but chairs and shade were plentiful on the beach. Staff members were there to round up participates for volleyball, water polo, soccer, dance lessons, etc. and local park reps walked around with parrots, snakes and monkeys to offer photo opportunities. The food was OK and there were plenty of choices between the buffets and Italian, Steakhouse, Seafood and Mexican restaurants. I did suffer some ntestinal distress?but can pinpoint the cause. We never had more than a 2 minute wait at any bar and the bartenders did not skimp on the top shelf rum whether we tipped or not with each drink order. Each hotel had a nightly show with semi professional dancers or a variety show with tourists supplying the fun. Some were entertaining, some were not. And finally, we did not see a single bug all week either in our room, on the beach or anywhere else.There are plenty of gift shops at the resort, but the prices are outrageous. My husband was about to purchase two small Snickers candy bars, but put them back when the cost as $10. And there is no Diet Coke anywhere in the country. CocaCola Lite is not the same as Diet Coke.We went to Punta Cana to relax, and so we did not go on any excursions outside of the resort.There were a few things that disappointed us, but these were not the fault of the resort. There was a constant 20 knot wind blowing all day and all night, for 8 days. The wind was strong enough to blow sand and this made it a little uncomfortable but not impossible to sit at the beach or to snorkel. Also, the first 50-75 feet of water at the beach were murky and not the crystal clean water shown in pictures. Apparently some local waterway had broken through barriers about a mile down the beach from our resort and was spilling into the ocean. We decided to swim in the pool instead of the ocean. Had we known about the condition of the water, we would have changed our reservations.We would consider returning to this resort but will pay closer attention to the tradewinds and ocean quality next time we travel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>read if you've never been to DR I have read many reviews and did my homework before booking my trip to the Dominican Republic. The single most important thing to prepare for if you have never been there is that it isn't going to compare to other caribbean islands. It is a third world country and you pay for what you get. Your best options are to pick resorts with a lot of options. Barcelo was good for this because you could go to all five hotels and use their facilities. The food was ok, but if you are a vegetarian an all-inclusive in DR aren't a good idea. The beach was absolutley amazing. I spent most of my trip on the beach and it made the trip worth while. They have a golf course but if your package doesn't include it it is a rip off. The cheapest sleeve of balls was $12 and they were crappy golf balls. In total it cost about $137 for nine holes for 2 people renting clubs and the course isn't that nice. Trust me here, I play a lot of golf. Overall, this place is a good choice for the Dominican Republic.

<Author>wilber305
<Content>Not Bad - Fun, but there are better choices I have been to other all-inclusive (Sandals Jamaica and Allegro Turks and Caicos) which I like better. However, you cant go wrong with an AI in the Caribbean ?we had a good time. I speak fluent Spanish which helps. I think for non-Spanish speakers they may have a better time in an in-inclusive in an English speaking country like Jamaica, Turks, etc. Not that many Americans at this resort, lots of Italians, Spaniards, Cubans from Miami and Latin Americans. The food was very varied, lots of choices of restaurants - I just didn like most of it - but I could always find something - so lots of steak and lobster for me. I don know why people recommend the Saona Island tour so much - I thought it was a rip-off. Long bus trip, then long boat trip to then just go to a beach on the island that is not that great.I Highly recommend the Jurassic Park tour. That was the best of the entire trip. Then they take you to a very gorgeous, beautiful beach (in Macao). Rigo, our guide was great. You learn alot about the country, etc. Free open bar the whole trip. This tour is awesome. Lots of fun.Take the little train shuttle to the Golf resort and play the free mini golf in the early evening. The people are all very nice ?lots of smiles.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Enjoyable! My wife  I are in our mid 30's, and this was our first all inclusive experience. I will tell it how it was, both positives  negatives.Hotel: The Caribe, pool,  grounds is better than the others (except the Palace 5*). We had problems with our door lock, safe, and where they put us. When we first arrived, they put us in the beach hotel (room far removed from everywhere). The next day requested a move to the Caribe  moved to the main level 50 metres from the pool, 20 metres from the beach. Maids cleaned  mopped the floors daily. Somtimes though, they cleaned the deck,  mosquitoes got into the room. The worst hotel experience happened to my wife. We were having a siesta, and my wife woke up screaming. A crab, the size of an egg, ended up on my wife's pillow snapping his claws while my wife slept. She awoke, I tossed the crab outside. We moved to a 2nd floor room the next day. As far as I can tell, the crab must have crawled under our door from the beach. The batteries from the door lock  safe occasionally went dead, and we at times found ourselves locked out of our room  safe at times during our stay. In summary, the rooms were older but clean. The rooms were probably the least desirable part of our trip.Food: Great! Itallian, Mexican, Beff Steakhouse,  there is a seafood lunch restaurant on the beach of Caribe. All great places to eat! Buffet restaurants (several) were good too. Overall, the food was fantastic, though it often did not agree with me. I felt bloated  had an upset stomach. The final day, I only ate toast, jam,  bananas.Grounds:Beautiful - endless beach - walk forever it seemed -north and east up the beach. Pools are nice. The pool at the Palace is the best, and there is less people. Chairs are always available.Shopping at the flea markets was sensational. I'm not a shopper, although I was during my trip. North east past the Palace along the beach is the flea market. The hotel guide says if you don't find them, they will find you. The # 7 jewelry booth was our favourite (if after jewelry). Antonio was the greatest guy. Raffael is nice too.There are also excursions (day-trips) that range from $50.00 to $85.00 U.S. funds. We went on the Isle Saona trip. This was the highlight! If we went again, we would have gone on several of these excursions. Well worth the money, as they are a lifelong memory. Canadian money can be exchanges to pesos, U.S. funds to pesos, but not Canadian funds to US funds. Exchange can be made at the front desk at a reasonable rate, although the best would be to complete all money exchange before you get to your holiday destination. Nightlife had nightly shows in all hotels, are all similar however, and we got tired of them.The people there are wonderful. Treat them nice. They always treated us nice.Finally, an overall rating (out of 5)Hotel rooms 3.0Food 3.5Grounds 4.5Native People 5.0Overall 4.0Would we go back to Dominican Republic? Yes. However, we would first look at other areas (Hawaii) to vacation. We would also choose other alternatives other than all inclusive. It seemed the food (developing country  all) was difficult to get used to (maybe too rich, though very delicious).Hope this helps all that visit the Dominican Republic

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>perfect weather nice resort! My husband and I stayed at this resort 4/17-4/24. The weather couldn't have been better! We had a great time. The resort grounds were absolutely beautiful so tropical and lush, perfectly landscaped. We choose the all-inclusive plan so you must wear a plastic bracelet all of your vacation which was no big deal. The rooms are modest but are kept very clean! We liked our balcony with a view of the pool and ocean. The airconditioner worked very well and kept our room cool and comfortable. We always left tips for the maid and also in-side the mini-bar which was filled daily with soda beer and water. We always brushed our teeth with the bottled water just in-case. Please bring with you everything you need because things are very expensive in the hotel store! Also reapply sunscreen very often. We were badly burned the first day and had to buy some aloe cool gel in the hotel store and they charged us $20 for a six dollar item in the states. There is shampoo,conditoner and soap in a dispenser in the shower but the quality is poor. The food is different then we were used to but we were always able to find something to eat. We would recommend the mexican restaurant,the steak house and the steak house pizza takeout. The margaritas in the mexican restaurant and the quesidillas are awesome! The bartenders at the little bars by the beach were the friendliest. Also the pool bar in the casino was our favorite bartender and also they have the best buffet. We defintely were the minority being from America but everyone seemed friendly. Yes there are many topless women but after the initial shock you have seen one you have seen them all. We did not try an excursion since we found plenty to do at the resorts. If you walk past the Barcelo rsort you will be bothered about time shares. There are people on the resort giving massages and braids but they don't hassle you. We were asked two or three times but once you say no they leave you alone. all-in-all we would rate this hotl a four star and we would return again. We perferred the atmosphere of the caribe over the beach resort. The pool was huge and never crowded. There were plenty of chairs on the beach where we spent most of our time. Go to this resort with confidence you won't be sorry!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Just Beautiful!!!!! My husband, 8 year old sin and I stayed at the Caribe 4/7 - 4/14. We are loyal cruiseship vacationers but this trip we decided to try the all inclusive and are completely satisfied. We booked the charter vacation and everything went smoothly. We were greeted at the airport and transferred directly to the hotel. There was some confusion as to which resort we were staying at. All my documents said Barcelo Bavaro Beach and Caribe, and our tranfers had Barcelo Bavaro Beach. We were dropped off at the Beach and were told we had the reservations for the Caribe. ( I had no idea they were two different hotels) The two hotels are right next to each other and just a 2 minute walk from lobby to lobby, but make sure when you are booking you are reserving the right hotel. Our rep also said that they are in the process of combining the two hotels which might make things a bit more confusing. During our stay, we did go to all the other resorts The Palace, Golf, Casino , and Beach. All very beautiful and easy to get to. We also did the Aquatic tour (speed boats and snorkels) which was great. This was my sons first time snorkeling, and our guide Raul was very patient and helpful getting him used to the equipment. We also went horse backriding. I recommend wearing long pants for this excursion. The sites were beautiful and relaxing. The horses took us through the golf course, the jungle and along the beach. I expected it to be very warm and hot, but it was actually cool and relaxing. The beach is turquise blue and absolutley beautiful. On most days we did not get to the beach until 1 or 2 pm. With our son we did not want to be in the high noon sun. The down fall with this is that most of the beach chairs were already taken. We did manage to find some abandoned ones, but it took time to look for them and drag them to our site. The beach is calm, with no large waves. We felt safe having my son play in the water. If you don't want to stay in direct sun, the beach is lined with palm trees which allows for many shady spots. My husband and I also got massages right on the beach in a little hut. It costs $20 for 30 minutes and very relaxing. The beach towels were unavailable later in the afternoon. I advise getting them early. We also spent $20 on a inflatable raft and $10 on a bucket and pail. If you have one bring it. If your going to do water sports, buy an underwater camera and pack it with you. Its way to expensive. OFF bug spray is a must. Those mosquiteos come out at night and since most of the restauraunts and theaters are outdoors, you will get bitten. Bring an anti itch cream too, We spent $12 at the gift shop for some caladryl that was definetly needed. The staff are friendly and helpful they make you feel very comfortable. As far as making purchases, if at all possible stay away from bringing large denomination bills. When you use them to pay for merchandise, they give you peso's back. If you don't plan on spending it, your stuck taking it home because The hotels won't change them back to dollars. Be cautious of the LOCAL vendors on the beach, they will try to rip you off and may give you fake merchandise. My son wanted a shell necklace, and the guy was charging us $18. He refused to pay so much and the vendor wouldn't go lower than $10. When we went to the Plaza Dominicana (on the Barcelo Property) I found a similiar necklace for $7. We also took advantage of the all inclusive services. The nonmotorized water sports are readily available, Bars are ready to serve you with drinks, and food was easily accessible with variety especailly for a picky 8 year old. We all had an incredibly fun and relaxing time

<Author>Mother-of-3-boys
<Content>Great Family Vacation Best Family Vacation we've ever had! We stayed at the Barcelo Bavaro Beach Resort during spring break from April 3rd to April 9th. Our boys 15, 12 and 11 had plenty to do and were never bored. We purchased wind surfing lessons for them which was a great deal. The instructor spent half the day in the water teaching the kids. Once they learned how to do it, they were able to use the sail boards when ever they wanted free of charge.The food reminded me of cruise ship food. It was satisfactory with some meals being better than others. The greatest thing about the food was I never had to worry about feeding my kids. They ate when they felt like eating and everyone found something they liked. Although the travel agent said not to tip, I think we got much better service when we left a dollar here and there.My 12 year old son made the mistake of brushing his teeth with the tap water and did get sick. Fortunately, there is a health clinic at the resort. The two young beautiful doctors were very kind and took excellent care of him. Our bill for the visit plus medications came close to about $200. After about 1 1/2 days he was able to enjoy the remainder of the vacation.I think the biggest eye openner and entertainment for my three American boys were the number of topless women walking along the beach. Actually, there was a small percentage of topless women, but it will probably be their greatest memory and the one they will talk about back at school.The beach was beautiful and the weather was perfect. It was also fun to sit by the pool and listen to live music and have drinks under the shade. I felt it was a safe atmosphere for the kids and very relaxing for the adults. I want to go back!!!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>It was Okay..... I spent one week in the Dominican Republic with my family for march break vacation. There were 9 of us. I have been to the Dominican 6 times in different parts of the island and I do have to say this. Punta Cana is my favorite. I also have to say this. This is my second time and the Barcelo Bavaro Beach and Caribe hotel and my experience was not the same as my past vacation. We were put into the 600 building, the Caribe, and I must say that the rooms could use some renovations. Other than that, I can't really complain. The weather was beatiful, the beach gorgeous, and the pools large and lots of fun. The food was not too bad, not great but like I said I have visited the D.R. many times so I knew what to expect. As you have probably read, there you can eat and play at al the hotels with the exception of the palace. For $20.00 U.S. you can eat tat the Chez Palace at the palace hotel and order anything off the menu. Drinks extra. That was worth the $20.00. There is a little choo-choo train that runs all day and night every 15 mntes to take you all over the resort, which is handy because sometimes i trains at night so if you want to go to a show or dinner at another hotel on the resort, you dont get wet. With the exception of the run down rooms in the 600 buildings, (The Caribe), the vacation was wonderful. I did check out the rooms at the palace, and they seem alot fresher and newer. All in all it was a good time! (good times, good times...)
